Fiberweb is a focused speciality industrial and construction 
materials business.
With vast experience in its field and a strong international 
presence, Fiberweb has long been regarded as a technological 
innovator with a strong portfolio of intellectual property and as a 
preferred partner for customers focused on high quality and 
reliable supply.

Manufacturing facilities 2    Fiberweb PLC  ANNUAL REPORT AND FINANCIAL STATEMENTS 2011 Fiberweb PLC  ANNUAL REPORT AND FINANCIAL STATEMENTS 2011    3  
Technical fabrics are used widely in many industrial 
markets. Fiberweb has a strong position in filtration, 
the construction industry, drier sheet and graphic arts 
markets amongst others.
In filtration, Fiberweb manufactures the well known 
Reemay
®
 brand of high-precision polyester fabrics as 
well as meltblown polypropylene filtration layers for 
facemasks and high-strength Typar
®
 polypropylene 
fabrics as support scrims. 
In the construction industry, Fiberweb manufactures 
fabrics for roofing applications.
In North America, consumers typically apply fabric 
softener to their clothes through the use of an 
impregnated drier sheet in a tumble dryer. This is a 
technically demanding application and Fiberweb is a 
leading supplier of the necessary substrate.
In the graphic arts industry, there is a demand for 
specialised wipes and roller covers used in the set-up 
of off-set lithographic printing processes and in more 
modern digital printing equipment. 
AGRICULTURE AUTOMOTIVE BUILDING DRIER SHEETS
FILTRATION GRAPHIC ARTS INDUSTRIAL SPECIALTY MEDICAL PRODUCTS
T echnical Fabrics
Geosynthetics comprises the Terram, Tubex and 
Boddingtons brands in the UK, the US, Australia and 
Germany and Fiberweb’s Typar
®
 housewrap, roofing 
and geotextile brand in the US and the global 
Defencell business.
The integration of the businesses and their respective 
brands, operating primarily in the UK and US with a 
strong background and proven excellence within the 
Civil, Building Construction, Military, Forestry and 
Horticulture and Landscaping sectors, offers 
enhanced commercial opportunities as well as 
adding value to existing customers through a 
significantly expanded product portfolio.

Geosynthetics Chairman’s Statement 
1
The most significant event of the year was the transformational 
sale of the majority of the Group’s hygiene nonwovens 
business to Petropar S.A. for an enterprise value of £229 
million representing an exit multiple of 6.2x underlying 2010 
EBITDA. The sale of around 40% of the Group, including six 
manufacturing sites in five countries with around 600 
employees, was a complex and challenging undertaking, 
demanding a great deal of management resource. Since 
2006, Fiberweb has struggled with a heavy inherited debt load 
and the need for significant investment. We have improved the 
hygiene business significantly through rationalisation and 
investments, took a major strategic step in 2009 with the 
formation of the FitesaFiberweb joint venture with Petropar 
and, with this disposal, have exited a commoditised and 
capital-intensive sector at an excellent price, leaving the  
Group debt-free. 
This transaction re-creates Fiberweb as a smaller, more 
tightly-focused specialty industrial and construction materials 
business, with particular competitive strengths in products for 
filtration, industrial processing, soil and construction 
engineering, drier sheets and several medical areas. With 
sales of some £300 million, eight manufacturing sites in six 
countries, and 1,200 valued employees, Fiberweb is well-
equipped to grow profitably in selected niche areas where high 
levels of technical and service differentiation are valued by 
customers. The £24 million proceeds of the rights issue in 
March, plus the £167 million immediately provided by the 
disposal have strengthened the balance sheet significantly, 
ensuring that we are well-placed to finance future growth and 
to exploit the uncertain economic environment that currently 
faces us. A further £17 million, including interest, is expected 
from Petropar at the end of 2012, when the 6% Vendor Loan 
Note that formed part of the consideration matures.
The two acquisitions made during 2011 underline our ability  
to execute our strategy for growth. Both Boddingtons, 
acquired in January 2011, and T ubex, acquired in May 2011, 
are specialised, niche businesses with strong market 
positions. They have enhanced Fiberweb’s existing T erram 
geotextile business, adding higher-margin, complementary 
products and allowing rationalisation of facilities and 
organisations. Both acquisitions are performing in-line with  
our expectations and post-acquisition rationalisation activities 
are almost complete, with two sites closing in the UK and 
T ubex production already commissioned at the Group’s  
Old Hickory site in the US.
The performance of our continuing business in 2011 was 
impacted by two significant operational issues: firstly, during 
the integration of T erram and Boddingtons, output and pricing 
issues at T erram hit margins and, secondly, during the planned 
relocation of activity from Königswinter to Berlin, it proved to 
be impossible to maintain adequate production resulting in 
delayed sales and yield reduction. While this is disappointing, 
following three years from 2008 to 2010 in which we delivered 
steady operational and margin improvement, both issues have 
largely been resolved and we expect steady improvement 
during 2012.
Financial results
The continuing Fiberweb Group, that is excluding the disposed 
hygiene business, produced sales of £297.8 million and 
underlying earnings before interest and taxes of £10.8 million. 
On an ongoing basis, with net cash and an anticipated tax 
charge of around 33%, this performance would have resulted 
in net earnings of around £6 million or roughly 3.4 pence per 
share. However, with the disposal occurring at the end of the 
year, the full interest costs of the debt that we had during the 
year are allocated to the continuing business and the actual 
tax credit applied reflects this interest cost and tax losses that 
have been capitalised during the year. As a result, the reported 
results indicate a net underlying loss after tax from continuing 
operations of £1.3 million (2010: £6.0 million profit) giving an 
adjusted loss of 0.8 pence (2010: 4.5 pence earnings) per 
share.
On a statutory basis, in 2011 the Group as a whole delivered 
profit after tax of £8.8 million (2010: £7.2 million), representing 
earnings per share of 5.3 pence (2010: 5.4 pence). The gain 
on disposal of the hygiene business was £1.5 million.
The results of the continuing business did not meet our 
medium-term goals for the continuing industrial-focused 
business of growth of around 2x GDP growth in our Western 
European and North American markets, 8-10% underlying 
PBIT
2
 return on sales and a return on capital employed of 
15%. However, there are many initiatives in the areas of cost 
reduction, operational improvement and innovation which are 
going to contribute significantly to delivering performance in 
line with our goals over the next few years.
The major financial events of 2011, notably the sale and 
operating leaseback of the large new utility plant 
commissioned at Old Hickory during 2010, the rights issue in 
March and the hygiene disposal, have resulted in a hugely-
strengthened balance sheet. This leaves us well positioned to 
finance further investments and also to consider possible 
acquisitions to accelerate the development of attractive 
elements of the business.
2011 was a watershed year for Fiberweb, with transformational change in our business 
portfolio and in the balance sheet. Operationally, while 2011 was a challenging year with a 
huge amount of corporate activity, we achieved several strategic objectives, and are now 
focused on the operational improvements necessary to deliver further value to shareholders. 
With a focused portfolio of attractive specialty industrial and construction materials 
businesses and a new, lean management structure, we have set new and attractive medium-
term financial goals and expect to make significant progress in 2012.
Malcolm Coster
Chairman

Dividends
The Board is pleased to recommend a final dividend at the 
expected level of 2.0 pence per share. This would give a total 
payout for 2011 of 3.0 pence per share, consistent with the 
stated objective at the time of the rights issue of keeping the 
distribution by the Company stable at around £5.2 million 
per annum. On the basis of the continuing business with a 
normalised tax and interest charge based on the post-disposal 
balance sheet, the dividend would be covered 1.1 times 
notwithstanding the operational issues that hit the results in 
2011. It is expected that the dividend will grow over time as 
performance improves, consistent with the stated policy of 
a minimum 30% payout of net earnings. The final dividend, 
if approved by shareholders, will be paid on 25 May 2012 to 
shareholders on the register on 27 April 2012 and the shares will 
go ex-dividend on 25 April 2012.
The board and Management
The Board remained unchanged during the year, though on  
3 January 2012 it was announced that Dan Abrams, CFO since 
2008, will leave the Company in March 2012. Dan has been 
central to the turnaround of the Group over the past 4 years and 
we thank him for his efforts and significant contributions during 
that time.
His place will be taken by Kate Miles. Kate has been with the 
Group for five years, firstly as Group Financial Controller and 
then as Finance Director of the Consumer Fabrics Division. 
Kate is a chartered accountant and her extensive experience 
at the Group, both in Head Office finance functions and as an 
operational finance director equip her ideally for her promotion 
to Group Finance Director.
Following the hygiene disposal, significant changes have been 
made to operational management in the Group. Most notably, 
Carsten Heldmann, previously President of the Consumer 
Fabrics Division, has been named Managing Director of 
Fiberweb T echnical Fabrics, while John Warner continues as 
Managing Director of Fiberweb Geosynthetics and has also 
assumed responsibility for the US-based T ypar housewrap and 
geotextile businesses. With the reduced scale of the Group, 
several central roles have been removed to ensure that the 
Group’s overhead structure is appropriate for its continuing 
business. These changes have been taking place from 
December 2011 and are likely to complete by mid-year 2012.
Prospects
Fiberweb’s strategy of developing and building on profitable, 
differentiated positions in niche industrial and construction 
materials should enable Fiberweb to achieve its medium-term 
financial goals and thereby deliver attractive returns to 
shareholders. The transformation of the Group’s balance sheet 
will allow these developments to be accelerated through 
increased management focus on a more attractive portfolio and 
through an improved ability to invest. Markets for specialty 
fabrics and materials in filtration, construction, medical devices 
and many other areas continue to grow, substituting for traditional 
materials and to improve energy, environmental and financial 
performance for customers. The Group’s prospects of exploiting 
attractive markets are excellent and we are well equipped to see 
the benefits of recent acquisitions, rationalisation and investment 
in technology and assets in 2012 and beyond.
Malcolm Coster 
Chairman
29 February 2012

Chief Executive’s Review
During 2011, we focused on improving our financial position, 
with the sale and operating leaseback of a new utility plant 
in the US in March, a rights issue in March to enable bolt-on 
acquisitions and finally the sale of the majority of our hygiene 
business in December. As a result, our gearing of 2.5x 
underlying
3
 earnings before interest, tax, depreciation and 
amortisation (EBITDA) at the beginning of January has been 
turned into a net cash position at the end of December.
We also completed two bolt-on acquisitions, with Boddingtons 
joining the Group in January 2011 and T ubex in May 2011, 
adding high-margin, specialty, complementary products 
to our existing, more commoditised T erram geotextiles 
business. The result of these activities has been to re-create 
Fiberweb at the end of 2011 as an international group with 
revenues of some £300 million, focused on developing and 
manufacturing specialty industrial and construction materials 
with particular strengths in products for filtration, industrial 
processing, soil and construction engineering, drier sheets 
and several medical areas. We have net cash of around £10 
million after covering all costs associated with the hygiene 
sale and hence enjoy a very strong financial position as we 
navigate the current economic uncertainties and volatility in 
raw material prices and seek to accelerate the development of 
our businesses.
The greater focus within our technologies and product 
offerings following the hygiene sale will assist us in driving 
operational improvement, reducing costs and increasing 
flexibility. 
Financial Performance
The reported Group financial results are significantly impacted 
by the accounting for the hygiene disposal which completed 
at the end of December 2011. These results are explained in 
detail in the Financial Review later in this report. The primary 
focus should be on the results of the continuing business.
Sales in the continuing Group of £297.8 million, up 11%, were 
broadly in–line with expectations, with volume growth of 3% 
including the benefit of acquisitions and a significant impact 
from pricing as rapid raw material cost increases in the first 
half fed through into price increases for Fiberweb products  
in the second half. Underlying operating profit reached  
£10.8 million, representing a return on sales of only 3.6%.  
This was disappointing and marks a temporary break with the 
trend of steady margin improvement seen from 2007 to 2010. 
The primary reasons for the shortfall against our plans were a 
delay in recovering raw material cost increases in our pricing, 
output and sales constraints arising from restructuring projects 
at Pontypool and Berlin and the absence of the raw material 
hedging profits seen in 2009 and 2010.
Operating cash flow at £20.5 million (2010: £37.7 million)  
was impacted by a working capital outflow of £9.8 million 
(2010: £4.3 million).
Return on capital employed, a key measure of the returns 
we are earning on shareholders’ capital, was driven lower 
by the reduced underlying operating profit from continuing 
operations to 5.6%. This is some way below our weighted 
average cost of capital and returning this crucial metric to an 
acceptable level above our estimated 10% long-term cost 
of capital is a key target for the coming period. This will be 
accomplished by improving margins through cost reduction, 
improving pricing and mix and seeking to improve our capital 
efficiency though reductions in working capital and tight 
control of capital expenditure.
For the discontinued hygiene business, sales were £210.8 
million, up 9.0% partly due to the impact of higher raw material 
prices on selling prices but also due to improved utilisation 
on the spunbond line commissioned in Italy during 2009. 
Underlying operating profit of £14.2 million, was up 75.3% due 
to a strong result from the FitesaFiberweb JV , cost reductions 
and yield improvements on several lines. The only area of 
significant weakness within Hygiene was the Chinese airlaid 
business, which continued to be impacted as in 2010, by 
volume weakness from its largest customer.
Retained profit for the year of £8.8 million (2010: £7.2 million) 
included a £1.5 million gain on disposal of the hygiene 
business.
 
Divisional Review
Technical Fabrics
T echnical Fabrics is a new division, created following the 
hygiene disposal from the previous Americas Industrial and 
Europe Industrial sub-divisions plus the retained drier sheet 
business at Old Hickory and the retained hygiene business in 
Europe at our sites at Biesheim, France and T erno d’Isola, Italy. 
T echnical Fabrics is much the larger of our two divisions and 
has five production sites in the USA, Germany, France and 
Italy with around 900 employees. The heart of our competitive 
(3)
 Before restructuring costs, amortisation of acquired intangibles and other non-recurring items.
The transformation of our portfolio and balance sheet during 2011 leaves us well-placed 
to grow our attractive specialty industrial materials businesses, to deliver strong returns 
for shareholders.
Daniel Dayan
Chief Executive  Fiberweb PLC  ANNUAL REPORT AND FINANCIAL STATEMENTS 2011    7  
We completed two bolt-on acquisitions, with Boddingtons 
joining the Group in January and Tubex in May 2011, adding 
high-margin, specialty, complementary products to our 
existing, more commoditised T erram geotextiles business. 8    Fiberweb PLC  ANNUAL REPORT AND FINANCIAL STATEMENTS 2011
strengths in T echnical Fabrics lies in specialty spunbond and 
conversion technology, such as Reemay nonwoven polyester 
fabrics, T ypar nonwoven polypropylene fabrics, Linopore film/
nonwoven laminates, Agryl, Novagryl and Covertan agricultural 
fabrics, polypropylene meltblown fabrics, and polyethylene 
nonwoven fabrics, carded hygiene and filtration fabrics.
Key events during 2011 included the commissioning of the new 
R&D centre and pilot line at Old Hickory, US, the completion 
of a new, large thermal and air-through bond carded fabric 
production line at T erno d’Isola, Italy and a significant upgrade 
of the breathable film and nonwoven line at Aschersleben, 
Germany. Sales were fairly stable, other than in European 
roofing where the disruption associated with the planned 
closure of the Blowitex site at Königswinter and transfer of 
production to Berlin caused delays to customer shipments and 
higher yield losses. Important steps have been taken in the 
development of new filtration fabrics, new fabrics for medical 
applications and in preparing the launch of a new Climat™ 
branded roofing product range in Europe.
Dr Carsten Heldmann assumed the leadership of the T echnical 
Fabrics Division in November, following the announcement of 
the hygiene sale. Carsten joined the Group in June 2005 as 
Head of Group R&D and following several years in R&D and 
Marketing management, primarily within the hygiene business, 
Carsten successfully led the Hygiene division from 2010 up 
until the disposal.
Geosynthetics
Geosynthetics is a new division, created from the Group’s 
existing UK-based T erram geotextile business, the two 2011 
acquisitions of Boddingtons and T ubex as well as the Group’s 
geotextile and construction businesses in the USA. From major 
sites at Maldon, Essex and Aberdare, South Wales in the UK, 
with around 300 employees, plus production at Old Hickory in 
the US, Geosynthetics now seeks to offer more complete and 
sophisticated solutions for civil engineering, rail engineering, 
drainage, ground stabilisation, landscaping and silviculture in 
the UK, Europe, the USA, Russia and the Middle East.  
The division is still young, but is aggressively moving towards 
solution selling and a more complete product offering in these 
areas.
Key events, other than the acquisitions themselves, include the 
commissioning in November 2011 of a T ubex tree shelter 
production line at Old Hickory, barely five months after T ubex 
was acquired, the ordering of a sophisticated new 
needlepunch production line to be installed at Maldon to 
strengthen the geotextiles offering in the UK, the restructuring 
of sites at Pontypool and Loddon as part of post-acquisition 
integration and the launch of improved synthetic roofing 
underlay products in the US housing market.
Much remains to be done to optimise the performance of this 
new division, with the closure of the final T erram line scheduled 
for mid-2012 following the successful commissioning of the 
needlepunch line at Maldon, strengthening of the sales team 
and new product initiatives in the rail industry. Customer wins in 
the US housing sector for our market-leading T ypar housewrap 
will support sales in this important market as it begins to 
recover after four years of recession, while tree shelter sales 
grew strongly in 2011 and are expected to continue developing 
well in 2012.
Our People
The entire Fiberweb team was challenged by a difficult and 
uncertain year. Restructuring at Pontypool, Maldon and 
Königswinter impacted many people. Around 600 employees 
left the Group together with the hygiene disposal and 
significant overhead cost reductions are now underway to 
reflect the smaller scale of the continuing business.  
In addition, the challenging economic environment also left its 
mark. In spite of these unsettling issues, Fiberweb people 
around the globe demonstrated commitment and 
determination to serve customers and shareholders alike.
The major management development programme –  
Fiberweb xL – launched last year has continued to prepare 
our most talented and committed staff from all functions and 
locations for new and greater challenges within Fiberweb as 
their careers develop. This two year programme should enable 
us to increase the proportion of senior vacancies we can fill 
internally and to increase the overall performance level of our 
senior management cadre.
Another major initiative developed further during 2011 was 
our in-house continuous improvement programme – Q5zero – 
targeting zero accidents, zero defects, zero late deliveries, zero 
inefficiencies and zero non-standard operations.  
More than one hundred people have now been trained in a 
five-module, five-week programme over a one-year period 
and we are beginning to see the benefits in a large number of 
individual improvement projects on our sites.
I would like to thank all Fiberweb employees for their 
commitment and creativity as we create a new Fiberweb as a 
growing and attractive industrial specialty materials business.
Outlook
Fiberweb’s performance is expected to improve significantly in 
2012, benefiting from the absence of the specific operational 
issues seen in 2011, from the increased focus on attractive 
niche, specialty markets and from the benefit of previous 
investment in assets, acquisitions, technology and marketing. 
The economic environment facing us is shifting, with some 
signs of recovery in the US, notably in the housing market, 
while Europe remains uncertain.
We enter 2012 with a strong balance sheet and the ability 
to accelerate our development. Strengthening our core 
businesses in filtration and specialty construction remains a 
priority and we need to consider establishing a meaningful 
presence in attractive emerging markets, which are likely to 
deliver the bulk of the global growth in our markets in the 
coming years. However, in the short-term we will concentrate 
on improving our operational performance, on continuing to 
reduce our overhead costs in line with the current scope of the 
Group and on reducing levels of working capital to drive up 
returns on capital employed. 
Daniel Dayan 
Chief Executive
29 February 2012

Business Review
Vision and Strategy
Fiberweb has a clear vision and strategy focused on 
using our materials technology and expertise to benefit 
customers. The strategy aims to create and sustain 
value for shareholders through a clear understanding 
of the needs of specialist niche markets and strong 
relationships with our customers. investment in 
production and application development ensures that 
Fiberweb has relevant, versatile and unique solutions to 
the ongoing challenges in these differentiated markets.

The technical fabrics market is diverse with an extremely 
wide range of end applications. Regional penetration, 
competition and potential growth can vary widely depending 
on the product areas and geography concerned.
Within technical fabrics, the nonwovens industry has grown 
steadily over the last three decades as these materials are 
increasingly used as a substitute for woven textiles and as 
products containing nonwovens have gained increasing 
penetration in emerging market areas. T echnological 
advances allow nonwovens to be used in new applications 
by improvements in properties such as strength, uniformity, 
flexibility, durability and permeability.
Markets
During the period under review Fiberweb operated in three 
main markets, namely hygiene, industrial and geosynthetics. 
Hygiene markets continue to exhibit, in general, the overall 
stable medium-term growth that has been seen in the past. 
The long-standing trend to lower basis weights (i.e. lighter 
fabrics) in response to rising raw material costs is expected 
to continue. The hygiene market, where steady 3-5% medium 
term growth is anticipated, is characterised by a 
concentrated and sophisticated customer base. Large 
multinational customers maintain very high standards of 
product quality and performance and expect nothing less 
from their suppliers. 
T echnological developments in the hygiene market towards 
better value products have continued to progress during 
2011 and are expected to be maintained in the medium-term. 
The drive to improve fabric performance at lower weight (i.e. 
with the use of smaller quantities of polymer) continues to be 
the most significant trend. There are also moves amongst 
some hygiene product producers to examine the use of 
sustainable raw materials.
The industrial and geosynthetics markets served by Fiberweb 
are varied and in most cases development has been as 
expected. The most difficult industrial market currently is  
the US residential construction market, with issues that have 
been well publicised. As a result of significant falls in new 
housing starts, market pressures have been considerable in 
housewrap and in construction-related areas of landscape 
fabrics and pool filtration. While measurements of market 
share are difficult, it is notable that Fiberweb experienced 
much lower volume declines than the fall in overall market 
demand as represented by new housing starts. A similar 
demand trend was also observed in European housing 
markets.
The industrial and geosynthetics markets are not only 
fragmented but the level of technical expertise and 
competition varies depending on the application. Key to 
success in these markets is the ability to respond rapidly 
and effectively to customer needs for improving value and 
performance, often at short notice.
Trends
2011 saw further significant volatility in the cost of Fiberweb’s 
most significant raw material, polypropylene. Polypropylene 
prices rose very rapidly in both North America and Europe 
during the first two quarters of the year, with relief only 
apparent mid-year in North America and in the autumn in 
Europe. A long-term trend of increasing oil prices and the 
knock on effect on polypropylene and the Group’s other 
major raw material, polyester, is expected to continue in the 
medium and long-term. We seek to manage this volatile 
situation through contractual pass-through arrangements 
as well as fixed price contracts and financial hedging 
arrangements where appropriate and reasonably priced. 
Hedging arrangements cannot always be put in place 
economically and, in these situations, Fiberweb needs to 
rely on pricing actions to maintain its margins where this 
is possible. In the industrial and geosynthetics markets, 
Fiberweb can in general move prices, subject to the 
competitive environment and agreements with customers,

while in the hygiene market, long-term raw material pass-
through contracts are typically in place with major customers 
accounting for around 80% of Fiberweb’s business in this 
sector during 2011. These pass-through contracts typically 
only allow quarterly adjustments to prices. Therefore, 
Fiberweb is typically exposed financially to the impact of at 
least three months’ increases in raw material costs. Another 
key trend impacting the hygiene business is the continued 
growth in emerging markets as the market penetration of 
disposable hygiene products continues to rise.
Following the sale of the majority of the Group’s hygiene 
business at the end of 2011, the Group’s raw material 
exposure has shifted significantly, with polyester now 
accounting for around 30% and polypropylene for around 
60% of raw material purchases, with other fibres accounting 
for most of the remainder.
The long-term growth of technical fabrics in industrial 
applications continues to appear to be secure, despite 
current negative pressures on volumes from the economic 
cycle. Demands for higher water and air quality continue 
to drive growth in filtration and demands for improved 
housing and infrastructure for much of the world’s population 
continue to drive the increased use of nonwovens in 
construction worldwide, both for housing and in the use of 
geotextiles in infrastructure for example.
external environment
The competitive environment of the technical fabrics 
and nonwovens industry is constantly changing, with 
technological innovations and the development of new 
markets and applications. Although Fiberweb had a strong 
position during the period under review with its broad 
product portfolio and global presence, it faced competition 
at various levels depending on the application, emphasising 
the need for continuing investment in research and the 
development of new products. There is a long-term trend 
towards consolidation in the nonwovens industry, as there 
can be advantages from scale, a broader geographic 
presence and a broader technology spread in meeting 
customer demands.
Description of Technical Fabrics business
In North America, Fiberweb operated in a number of areas in 
construction, filtration, landscape, furniture and bedding and 
specialities, with a single, large manufacturing site located in 
Old Hickory, US.
In construction, our major products are in housewrap, 
landscape and geotextile markets. Fiberweb’s Typar™ is the 
second largest brand for housewrap in North America.  
In Canada, Typar is the leading market brand for housewrap.
We are the market leader in pool and spa filtration under our 
strong brand Reemay™. Reemay is recognised by many 
as an industry standard in filtration markets, especially for 
pool and spa filtration and Fiberweb continues to work and 
improve the performance of these products to stay ahead 
of competition. Reemay is also used to make drier sheets 
for the North American consumer market, an attractive niche 
area of application in which Fiberweb has market leading 
technology. We also manufacture high performance products 
for use in the graphic arts industry, such as nil-scratch wipes 
and dampener covers.
In Europe, our T echnical Fabrics business is somewhat less 
developed than in North America. It falls into three main 
segments, namely construction, filtration and technical 
nonwovens and we also enjoy a presence in smaller 
segments for specialist medical fabrics and crop-cover in 
agricultural markets. In Europe, we focus on roofing, filtration, 
agriculture and speciality polyethylene-based fabrics.
In Asia, the group mainly sells small volumes of specialist 
Reemay filtration fabrics and Typar for various construction 
applications.

Description of Geosynthetics business
Our Geosynthetics business comprises the T erram™, 
Boddingtons™ and Tubex™ product ranges. Since the 
disposal of our hygiene business our Geosynthetics 
business also incorporates our North American construction 
business.
In the UK, our site in Maldon, Essex produces branded 
geotextiles under the T erram and Boddingtons brands with 
a strong market position in the UK, as well as speciality 
geosynthetics and constructions for a variety of applications, 
including in the rail and defence industries. The business is 
also served by sales offices in Minneapolis in the US and 
Leipzig in Germany. Significant quantities of geosynthetic 
products are exported from the UK to markets in Europe, 
Russia and the Middle East.
At Aberdare in South Wales, a variety of tree shelter products 
are manufactured for sale in silviculture and viticulture 
markets in the UK and Europe. During 2011, production of 
tree shelters commenced at our facility in Old Hickory, US to 
improve access to North American markets.
Description of Hygiene business 
The hygiene business provides nonwoven fabrics to 
major consumer goods companies around the world for 
applications in baby care and feminine hygiene. These are 
produced using two principal methods, namely spunbond 
and airlaid technology.
In North America, Fiberweb produced carded thermal bond 
material which is used principally for extensible applications 
such as ears and side panels in baby diapers and spunbond 
and spunmelt materials as components for diapers and 
feminine care products. During the period under review, 
Fiberweb’s manufacturing sites were located in the US 
in Simpsonville and Green Bay. Fiberweb also owned a 
50% stake in the FitesaFiberweb joint venture which had 
manufacturing sites located in Washougal and Simpsonville 
in the US and in Mexico and Brazil.
In Europe, Fiberweb held a market leading position as a 
result of continuous investment across manufacturing sites 
in France, Germany, Italy and Sweden. At our Chinese facility 
based in Tianjin, we produced advanced airlaid material 
for absorption and/or distribution of liquid for use in the 
manufacture of disposable feminine hygiene products.  
In Asia, Fiberweb was the largest airlaid roll goods producer, 
supplying most of the leading feminine care producers in the 
region as well as the European market.
On 30 December 2011, Fiberweb completed the sale of the 
majority of its hygiene business to Petropar S.A. The sale 
included sites located in Simpsonville and Green Bay in the 
US, Norrköping in Sweden, Trezzano Rosa in Italy, Peine in 
Germany and Tianjin in China. The sale also included 
Fiberweb’s 50% stake in the FitesaFiberweb joint venture 
which owned sites in Washougal and Simpsonville in the US 
as well as in Mexico and Brazil. This sale will allow Fiberweb 
to become a focused leader in certain attractive segments of 
the growing technical fabrics and construction products 
markets, with leading positions in several attractive market 
and technology niches, notably in filtration, construction 
specialties, geosynthetics, agriculture and several medical 
areas. Following the sale, Fiberweb created the new T echnical 
Fabrics Division comprising the current Americas Industrial 
and Europe Industrial units, including the Old Hickory drier 
sheet business and the remaining hygiene sales from 
Fiberweb’s sites in Biesheim, France and T erno d’Isola, Italy.

Research and development
The primary purpose of Fiberweb research and 
Development is to provide innovation to Fiberweb’s 
customers by optimising the performance of existing 
products and processes and by developing new, more 
cost efficient solutions.
 
For our T echnical Fabrics Division, Fiberweb’s R&D efforts 
continue to focus on spunbond and meltblown platform 
technologies, product innovations, portfolio depth and 
breadth, new markets and manufacturing processes.  
Recent developments include the following:
>
The creation of a new portfolio in synthetic 
roof underlayment. It includes a new 
Surround SR™ roofing product and a new 
premium roofwrap.
>
The commercialisation of a new pool and 
spa media.
>
The creation of a highly uniformed 
Reemay (2 – 5x) product with properties 
suitable for a platform of liquid filtration 
media applications.
>
The development of a new  
FFP1-3 class respiratory mask media 
range offering extra low breathing 
resistance to increase comfort for the end 
user.
>
The development of a new F7-F9 
class HVAC (Heating, Ventilation, Air 
Conditioning) media range complying with 
the new European Standard EN779:2011.
On the research front, we are evaluating nanofibers, 
modelling filtration efficiency and employing computational 
fluid dynamics to advance our process innovation.
In our hygiene businesses, focus was given to developing 
innovative nonwovens with better softness and improved 
surface, extensibility, strength and absorbency properties, 
which, in addition to sustainability, are the key attributes that 
our hygiene customers are requesting. Recent developments 
include the following:
>
Line optimisation and waste reduction 
– rising raw material costs and strong 
competitive pressure have led to several 
activities focussed around operational 
improvements. A global operations 
improvement team has been formed with the 
aim of implementing several programmes in 
2012 targeted towards waste reduction and 
line operational efficiency. 
>
Softness – new polypropylene based resin 
blends consisting of technically advanced 
composites of special copolymers and 
melt additives which provide enhanced 
drape and feel. In addition we have 
designed a new spunbond process 
that provides nonwovens from crimped 
filaments creating a pleasant bulk and 
“cotton-like” touch.
>
Bico fibres – new bi-component products 
based on exclusive composites of resins 
and advanced modifiers which provide 
improved softness and permanent 
hydrophilic properties.  Fiberweb PLC  ANNUAL REPORT AND FINANCIAL STATEMENTS 2011    19

Research and development continued
Whereas R&D focuses on upstream product and process 
development and important new platform technologies, 
T echnical Services (“TS”) provides local technical support 
to our customers. Being close to customers and their needs 
enables us to anticipate new market trends and is a key 
element of this function. The R&D and TS Departments work 
closely together and responsibility for these aspects of product 
and process development is co-ordinated globally between 
the respective departments in Europe, the US and Asia.
Overall, Fiberweb continues to invest significantly in R&D 
to maintain its leading market positions as is shown by our 
major investment in our R&D Centre at our Old Hickory, 
T ennessee plant. This pilot facility will be our Centre of 
Applications Excellence and Customer Innovation. In addition 
to the state of the art area bonded nonwoven machine,  
we are upgrading a coex extrusion coating line and a 
composite lamination line. T o complement the converting 
capability, advanced downstream equipment to simulate 
customer applications will be acquired, along with new 
analytical instrumentation. A grand opening of the centre is 
scheduled for the first half of 2012.
>
Dryness – new durable hydrophilic spin 
finishes which resist multiple wetting and 
offer improved dryness in diaper top 
sheets and inner layers.
>
Extensibility – significant progress has 
been made towards the qualification of 
proprietary, highly extensible spunbond 
nonwovens.
>
Light weight and high strength – an 
improved spinning process which enables 
the spinning of finer fibres with improved 
strength in order to produce a lower 
weight fabric.
>
Airlaid products – several new airlaid 
products were launched in 2011, such 
as, an ultra thin absorbent core, super 
absorbing fibres that provide higher 
acquisition speeds, zero spillage and near 
100% homogeneous distribution, and a 
hybrid airlaid core comprising a synthetic 
acquisition layer.
>
Sustainability – investigations into new 
sustainable raw materials have become 
more important for the Company in order 
to develop green nonwoven products 
with smaller carbon footprints including 
biodegradable products which are more 
environmentally friendly.
>
International research collaboration – a 
long-term collaboration and partnership 
with the University of Cambridge has been

review of results
The prior year results have been restated to show the 
results of the disposed Hygiene business as a discontinued 
operation. Following the disposal, Fiberweb has revised its 
segmental structure to create two new segments:
q 	 T echnical Fabrics 
q 	 Geosynthetics
The T echnical Fabrics division includes revenues of £101.3 
million (2010: £87.1 million) in respect of retained businesses 
formerly included within the Group’s Hygiene division.
Revenue
 
Revenue – continuing operations increased by 11%
Revenue from continuing operations increased by 11% to 
£297.8 million (2010: £269.2 million). At constant currency 
sales increased £30.9 million (12%) above the prior year.  
This reflects the 3% volume increase and the impact on 
prices of the higher raw material prices in the first half.
The T echnical Fabrics division experienced an overall volume 
increase of 1%. Volumes in Europe were flat, with a year-on-
year increase in the US of 2% primarily driven by Drier Sheet. 
In revenue terms, total division sales increased by 7% overall 
to £234.5 million. 
Revenue – Technical Fabrics increased by 7%
Within Geosynthetics, volumes increased 15% year on 
year reflecting the contribution from the Boddingtons and 
Tubex acquisitions during the year. Like-for-like sales, after 
adjusting for the impact of acquisitions, reduced by 13% to 
£43.9 million, primarily due to continued weakness in the 
US construction market. Boddingtons contributed sales of 
£16.1 million and Tubex contributed sales of £3.3 million post 
acquisition. 
Revenue – Geosynthetics increased by 25%
Within discontinued operations, Hygiene volumes reduced 
by 1% compared to 2010, whilst sales were up by 9% 
reflecting higher raw material prices. Hygiene sales revenues 
are impacted by the contractual pass through arrangements 
for raw material prices, which distorts the relationship with 
underlying trading volumes. On a constant currency basis, 
sales of £210.8 million were 6% higher than the prior year. 
Revenue – discontinued operations increased by 9%
Underlying Operating Profit
Underlying Operating Profit reduced to £10.8 million
Underlying operating profit of £10.8 million in the continuing 
group was disappointing against £20.9 million in the prior 
year. Underlying margins fell from 7.8% in 2010 to 3.6% 
in 2011. In the first half of 2011, the underlying margin 
was 5.0% (2010: 9.0%) and was impacted by a delay in 
recovering the sharp raw material cost increases in our 
pricing as well as the operational issues in Pontypool. In the 
second half, the underlying margin fell to 2.2% (2010: 6.4%) 
as a result of volume weakness in Southern Europe and US 
construction markets, and also the impact of the integration 
activities in Berlin following the closure of the Königswinter 
site, where delays in commissioning a new line disrupted 
order fulfilment. In addition, the benefits arising from raw 
material hedging in 2010 were not repeated, particularly in 
the second half of 2011 when a loss of £1.5 million arose on 
hedging compared to a profit of £5.4 million in the full year  
in 2010.
Technical Fabrics margins reduced to 8.8%
T echnical Fabrics underlying margins reduced from 13.8%  
to 8.8% reflecting the operational issues in Berlin in the 
second half and increased raw material prices at the start 
of the year which were not adequately recovered in selling 
prices. Underlying margins reduced to 5.8% in the second 
half compared to 11.6% in the first half and 13.8% in the 
second half of 2010, largely due to the output and yield 
problems suffered in Berlin together with a second half 
hedging loss of £1.5 million. Berlin operations are now 
substantially recovering, and optimal yields and customer 
service are expected to be re-established through the first 
half of 2012.
Geosynthetics margins reduced to (5.7)%
Geosynthetics underlying margins reduced to (5.7)% in 
2011 from (3.0)% in 2010. Underlying margins improved 
from (11.7)% in the first half to (0.2)% in the second half 
reflecting the resolution of the first half operational issues 
at T erram which affected pricing and output and the impact 
of price increases. Underlying operating margins in the 
acquired Boddingtons and Tubex businesses are healthy 
and in line with expectations. T otal divisional margins were 
adversely impacted by the ongoing weak demand in the US 
construction markets and the consequent impact of surplus 
capacity on overhead recovery.

Within discontinued operations, the FitesaFiberweb joint 
venture continued to trade strongly. In Hygiene, the sharp 
increase in raw material prices in the first half of 2011 
coupled with the contractual lag in pass-through impacted 
margins in the first half, although there was some mitigation 
from operational improvements. There was a strong 
performance in the second half as a result of the contractual 
pass-through and decreasing raw material costs. 
Raw Materials
Raw material costs are a significant cost component 
representing approximately 53% of Group continuing revenues 
in 2011. They are largely dictated by external factors including 
the oil price, from which propylene and polypropylene are 
derived, as well as demand and capacity issues at various 
points along the petrochemical supply chain. 
Polypropylene prices increased sharply by about 18% in the 
first half of the year, and then declined and stabilised during 
the second half of 2011 resulting in an overall decrease of 
circa 6% across the year. The Group actively manages the 
volatility caused by movement in raw material prices with 
hedging transactions. The impact of these arrangements was 
a loss of £0.9 million in 2011 (2010: a gain of £5.4 million), with 
a small profit in the first half offset by losses of £1.5 million in 
the second half of the year. In 2011, the net adverse impact of 
raw material price increases on the total group after hedging 
and contractual pass-through was £3.8 million.
Historically some 50% of Group revenues were subject to 
contractual pass-through arrangements, comprising the 
majority of Hygiene business revenues. There are more limited 
contractual pass-through arrangements in the T echnical 
Fabrics and Geosynthetics segments and raw material price 
risk is addressed through hedging activities and pricing 
activities with customers and on occasion, hedging activities.
In the future, approximately 40% of the Group’s revenues 
(primarily the retained hygiene businesses) will remain 
subject to contractual pass-through, with the balance of 
industrial volumes dependent on negotiated pricing action to 
recover raw material volatility. The Group’s raw material mix is 
now less dependent on polypropylene than in the past, with 
polyester playing a relatively more important role than before.
Restructuring Costs, Amortisation of Acquired Intangibles 
and other Non-Recurring Items
Restructuring costs, amortisation of acquired intangibles and 
non-recurring items for continuing operations totalled £2.1 
million (2010: £3.6 million). Restructuring costs of £7.2 million 
arose primarily from the integration of the acquired Boddingtons 
and T ubex businesses and the transfer of production from the 
Königswinter site in Germany to Berlin, together with costs 
incurred to reflect the smaller scope and sale of the business as 
a result of the Hygiene disposal. These costs were partially 
compensated by a gain of £2.6 million (2010: £0.6 million) on 
the disposal of previously impaired assets from our Korma site 
in Italy following its closure.
Within cost of sales, impairment charges of £1.6 million 
(2010: £Nil) were recognised relating to some obsolete 
equipment in Italy and assets in Geosynthetics no longer 
required as a result of the transfer of production to Maldon. 
£0.4 million of additional costs were incurred on the disposal 
of Old Hickory utility plant. In 2010, a charge of £0.6 million 
was recorded on the transfer of the Old Hickory utility plant as 
held for sale to reflect fair value less costs to sell.  
The Group recognised losses of £0.7 million on the ineffective 
portion of the mark-to-market valuation adjustment in respect 
of polypropylene hedges (2010: gains of £0.7 million). 
Within administrative expenses, a curtailment gain and 
immediate recognition of past service cost credit of £6.4 
million within continuing operations, with a further gain of 
£2.0 million in discontinued operations, arose following 
changes made to benefits under our US post retirement 
medical benefit plan. £0.3 million of transaction costs and 
related professional fees were incurred primarily associated 
with the acquisition of Boddingtons and Tubex (2010: £3.7 
million). In addition, a charge of £0.3 million arose on the 
impairment of the Group’s investment in Cordustex (Pty) 
Limited. The amortisation of acquisition related intangible 
assets was £0.6 million (2010: £Nil).
Within discontinued operations, non-recurring costs of £2.0 
million were incurred. An impairment charge of £3.0 million 
was recognised following the decision to close the Fiberweb 
T echnical NonWovens business in China. Restructuring costs 
of £1.7 million were incurred across the business. This was 
offset by the post retirement medical plan changes of £2.0 
million referred to above and £0.7 million of gains on the sale 
of land in Simpsonville, US and Peine, Germany.
Acquisitions
The acquisition of the Boddingtons group of companies was 
successfully completed on 6 January 2011. The Tubex group 
of companies was acquired on 17 May 2011. The integration 
of these companies into the Geosynthetics segment is 
progressing well and the operations are performing in line 
with expectations. A new needlepunch geotextile production 
line in Maldon is expected to be operational in the first half 
of 2012, which will allow the final closure of the old T erram 
facility in Pontypool and complete the post-acquisition 
integration programme.

Disposal of the Hygiene Business
The disposal of the Hygiene business completed on 30 
December 2011 for a total consideration of $286 million 
(including the issue of a 6% Vendor Loan Note of $26 
million). Disposal costs of £8.8 million included transaction 
costs of £6.5 million, and £1.8 million accelerated write-down 
of the prepaid facility fees in connection with the repayment 
of the Group’s Revolving Credit Facility (“RCF”) in January 
2012. Disposal costs also include other finance costs relating 
to the break fees on early repayment of the RCF and the 
crystallisation of £1.2 million on the mark-to-market of interest 
rate swaps held against the RCF debt which were settled 
in January 2012 offset by the immediate recognition of past 
service costs on the post retirement medical benefit scheme 
of £0.8 million as a result of the disposal. 
Net Cash
Net Cash of £22.0 million
Following the disposal of the Hygiene business, the Group 
had net cash of £22.0 million at the year end (2010: net debt 
of £151.2 million). This is expected to reduce to around £10 
million after payment of disposal transaction costs and related 
restructuring costs. The Group had previously set a target of 
reducing net debt to a maximum of two times EBITDA over the 
medium term. This has now been achieved. The proceeds of 
the disposal were used to pay down the outstanding amounts 
due under the RCF at the beginning of January 2012. As a 
result of this repayment, the Group’s interest rate swaps were 
terminated. Following the disposal of the Hygiene Business on 
30 December 2011, the loan facility was reduced to £50 million 
comprising multi-currency facilities of €30 million and US$40 
million. Other terms remain unchanged.
As part of the proceeds for the disposal of the Hygiene 
business, the Group issued a one-year Vendor Loan Note to 
Petropar for $26 million at a coupon rate of 6% payable on 
redemption on 30 December 2012.
Interest Charge and Borrowings 
Net finance costs for continuing operations were £15.9 million 
(2010: £14.8 million). The higher costs reflect a full year of the 
new RCF facility established in July 2010 which has a higher 
margin than the previous facility. No allocation of interest 
charges relating to the Group’s RCF has been made to 
discontinued operations on the basis that debt and these 
costs are managed on a group basis and cannot meaningfully 
be directly allocated. Following the repayment of the 
outstanding balances under the RCF with the proceeds of the 
Hygiene disposal, net finance costs are expected to be 
significantly reduced in future. The most material elements of 
the ongoing interest charge will be non-cash pension interest 
on the Group’s pension deficit, offset in 2012 by the interest to 
be received on the Vendor Loan Note.
Profit Before Tax
Underlying loss before tax from continuing operations
After net finance costs of £15.9 million (2010: £14.8 million), 
Fiberweb generated an underlying loss before tax from 
continuing operations of £5.1 million (2010: £6.1 million profit). 
Profit before tax for discontinued operations was £11.7 million 
excluding the gain on disposal (2010: £4.6 million). The gain 
on disposal before tax was £8.9 million.
Taxation
The Group recorded a net tax credit for the year on 
underlying profits from continuing operations of £3.8 million 
(2010: £0.1 million charge). The Group recognised a net 
credit of £3.0 million (2010: £3.6 million) in respect of the final 
recognition of deferred tax assets in respect of historic US 
losses, partial recognition of deferred tax assets on UK and 
Italian tax losses and other timing differences. The Group 
now has full recognition of the deferred tax assets in the US 
following the fourth profitable year in the US since demerger, 
with forecast profitability now underpinning the Group’s 
ability to benefit from brought forward tax losses as we move 
ahead. In addition, deferred tax assets have been partially 
recognised on historic UK and Italian losses as a result of 
forecast future profitability.
Excluding the deferred tax credits, the underlying tax  
credit was £0.8 million (2010: £3.7 million charge), 
representing an underlying effective tax rate of 15.7% (2010: 
60.7%). The high rate in 2010 reflected the fact that no benefit 
was recognised on UK tax losses in the year. A tax charge of 
£7.4 million arose on the disposal of the hygiene business.

Underlying operating margins in the continuing group have 
reduced to 3.6% from 7.8% last year reflecting the impact of 
the operational issues at Berlin and Pontypool as a result of 
the restructuring initiatives. 
Earnings growth was negative as a result of the operational 
issues at Pontypool and Berlin, with continuing adjusted 
EPS at (0.8) pence per share (2010: 4.5 pence per share). 
Excluding the deferred tax credit of £3.0 million (2010: £3.6 
million) in respect of historic tax losses, the adjusted loss  
per share was 2.6 pence (2010: earnings per share 1.8 
pence). 
Return on Capital Employed (ROCE) reduced from 13.7% to 
5.6% a result of the reduction in operating profit. ROCE, defined 
as underlying operating profit from continuing business in the 
last 12 months against total fixed assets and working capital, is 
considered an appropriate measure against which to monitor 
the Group’s improving performance.
Revenue from continuing operations increased by 10.6%. 
This reflects the 3% increase in volumes and the higher raw 
material prices during the year, as well as the impact of the 
Boddingtons and Tubex acquisitions (£19.4 million). In the 
prior year, revenue from continuing operations increased by 
5.9%. 
An important KPI in managing the operating cash of 
the business is trading working capital expressed as a 
percentage of annualised sales, which, at the year end 
was 15.4% (2010: 13.1%). The Group continues to target 
reductions in working capital as a percentage of revenue. 
Operating cash flow, a critical measure, was £20.5 million 
(2010: £37.7 million). This reflects a working capital increase 
of £9.8 million (2010: £4.3 million). 
Cash Flow, Net Debt and Liquidity 
Net cash from operating activities was £20.5 million (2010: 
£37.7 million). The net cash inflow in the year was £156.2 
million (2010: £2.6 million) reflecting the net proceeds 
of the Hygiene disposal offset by £23.4 million of capital 
expenditure (2010: £33.2 million), £9.4 million of net interest 
payments (2010: £8.0 million) and shareholder dividends of 
£6.0 million (2010: £5.2 million). 
Cash from operating activities was impacted by a working 
capital outflow of £9.8 million (2010: £4.3 million working capital 
outflow). Other adjustments to operating cashflow include 
pension contributions of £4.9 million (2010: £4.3 million), 
including a one off contribution of £0.6 million in the US, and 
tax payments of £3.4 million (2010: £0.3 million).
Capital investment of £23.4 million includes £18.3 million in 
the continuing group (2010: £33.2 million; £25.2 million in 
the continuing group) and continues to secure competitive 
manufacturing and product development infrastructure for 
the future. The major capital projects during 2011 were the 
significant upgrade of the breathable film and nonwoven 
line at Aschersleben, Germany; a new thermal and air-
through bond carded fabric production line at T erno d’Isola, 
Italy; a new roofing membrane line in Berlin and additional 
investment at the new R&D centre in the US. The Old Hickory 
utility plant, which was successfully commissioned in August 
2010, was sold and leased back under an operating lease in 
March 2011. 
The rights issue generated net cash proceeds of £23.8 
million. In addition, net proceeds of £18.3 million were 
received on the sale and operating lease back of the Old 
Hickory utility plant, land at the Simpsonville and Peine sites, 
the land and buildings at Königswinter in Germany following 
the transfer of the business to Berlin and on the disposal 
of previously impaired assets from our Korma site in Italy 
following its closure.
Dividends of £1.6 million were received from the 
FitesaFiberweb joint venture prior to its disposal.
The net cash outflow on the acquisitions of Boddingtons and 
T ubex was £7.9 million (2010: £Nil). The net cash inflow on 
the disposal of the Hygiene business in the year was £161.2 
million. The majority of the £8.8 million related costs, including 
the swap termination costs, will be paid in 2012.
Treasury 
The Group’s policy is to hedge its interest exposure and 
entered into interest rate hedges for its exposure to both US 
Dollar and Euro floating interest rates under its loan facility 
(“RCF”). During the year, these interest hedges accounted 
for more than 70% of the debt under the RCF . Following 
the repayment of the RCF debt with the proceeds from the 
Hygiene business disposal, the swaps were terminated and 
settled in January 2012.
During the year, the RCF debt was used as a translation 
hedge against net operating assets. There is limited 
transactional exposure as there is relatively little trading 
across currency borders. The bulk of raw material sourcing 
and other purchases are in the currency of operation, and 
the total volume of the Group’s business which is affected by 
relative currency movements is less than 10% of its turnover. 
It is the Group’s policy to hedge those exposures which are 
material for a period of up to 12 months, using a specified 
range of financial instruments.

Following the disposal of the Hygiene business, the Group is 
in a net cash position and no longer has Swedish Krona 
assets and therefore any future drawdowns are likely to be in 
US Dollar or Euro.

Credit Risk
The Group has a history of limited bad debts and it is  
believed its major customers are of good credit quality.  
Credit insurance is used in most markets. However, the 
inevitable consequence of the recent recessionary 
environment means that the Group will increasingly assume 
balance sheet risk for some trading customers for whom credit 
insurance is either restricted or unavailable. The Group adopts 
a prudent policy for reviewing and advancing credit and for 
ensuring adequate provision for bad debts. 
Shareholder Fund Movements
The Group has equity of £178.8 million (2010: £178.6 
million). Of these reserves, £27.9 million (2010: £76.2 million) 
are distributable reserves. The reduction in distributable 
reserves is a result of the disposal of the Hygiene business.
Retirement Benefits
The major retirement benefits and pension schemes are now 
defined contribution schemes. The Group retains responsibility 
for the scheme deficit in the Simpsonville and Washougal 
pension schemes in the US which are now frozen. During the 
year, changes were made to the Group’s post retirement 
medical benefits schemes in the US resulting in a curtailment 
gain of £0.6 million and immediate recognition of past service 
cost gains of £5.8 million in continuing operations.
The net pension liability is calculated by the Group’s actuaries, 
and is based on the fair value of the schemes’ assets and the 
present value of the schemes’ liabilities. This net liability 
reduced by £9.0 million during the year to £26.5 million (2010: 
£35.5 million), with total curtailment gains and past service 
credit recognition of £9.3 million offsetting actuarial losses of 
£9.3 million incurred primarily as a result of changes in the 
long-term discount rates applied to the US obligations. 
Liabilities of £5.9 million were disposed as part of the disposal 
of the Hygiene business comprising the Simpsonville post 
retirement medical benefit scheme and the defined benefit 
schemes in Corovin and Fiberweb Italy. Contributions paid 
totalled £4.9 million (2010: £4.3 million). Non-cash net interest 
on pension liabilities was £1.4 million (2010: £1.7 million).

Principal Risks & Uncertainties 
The following are the most significant risks identified by the 
Board and management:
1. Raw material costs
Raw materials represent the single most important input for 
the Group’s production, representing approximately 53% of 
sales in 2011. Although there are a variety of raw materials 
used by the Group, the key raw materials are polypropylene 
and polyester. The prices of polypropylene and polyester are 
volatile and depend primarily on the price of crude oil and 
monomer and polymer manufacturing capacity and demand. 
There is therefore a material exposure to movements in raw 
material prices. Significant increases in raw material prices 
that cannot be passed on to customers could have a material 
adverse effect on the Group’s results and financial condition.
Historically, increases in the price of polypropylene in 
particular have put pressure on the Group’s margins. Prior to 
the disposal of the Hygiene business, the Group was subject 
to contractual pass-through arrangements on approximately 
50% of revenues whereby polypropylene price increases or 
decreases are passed on to its customers. These pass-
through arrangements were generally subject to a time lag of 
up to three months. 
There are more limited contractual pass-through arrangements 
in the T echnical Fabrics and Geosynthetics segments, with 
approximately 40% of the Group’s continuing revenues 
remaining subject to contractual pass through protection.  
As a result, the Group actively manages the volatility caused 
by movement in raw material prices with hedging transactions 
and through strategic alliances with polypropylene producers.
2. Customer and supplier dependency
Historically, across certain markets in which the Group 
operates there was a high degree of dependency on 
maintaining good relationships with a relatively small number  30    Fiberweb PLC  ANNUAL REPORT AND FINANCIAL STATEMENTS 2011
of key customers. The failure of the Group and its key 
customers to renew contracts could result in a significant 
reduction in the demand for its products. This was 
particularly the case for Procter & Gamble which, through a 
large number of different contracts and purchasing 
arrangements of varying durations, accounted for 
approximately 23% of total sales in 2011. In terms of overall 
concentration, the Group’s top ten customers accounted for 
47% of total sales in 2011. Following the Hygiene disposal, 
Petropar SA will be both a key customer and supplier to the 
Group. The failure of one or more of these key customers 
could therefore have a material adverse effect on the 
Group’s reputation, business, results of operations and 
overall financial condition. 
The Group has procedures in place to monitor and mitigate 
this risk and, historically, has been generally successful in 
agreeing new contracts with key customers or extending 
existing contracts. Following the disposal of the Hygiene 
business, Fiberweb’s concentration of customers has reduced 
and Proctor & Gamble represents 11% of the continuing 
group sales. The top 10 customers of the continuing group 
represented only 32% of continuing sales in 2011.
Similar dependency arises in respect of maintaining regular 
supplies of polypropylene and other resins and fibres.  
The Group is reliant on a small number of critical suppliers in 
the global market. Given the limited alternative suppliers, a 
disruption in the supply chain could lead to the Group being 
unable to satisfy the needs of its customers. The failure of  
one or more of the Group’s key suppliers could therefore 
have a material adverse effect on the Group’s reputation, 
business, results of operations and overall financial condition. 
The Group seeks to mitigate this risk through diversity of 
supply and by negotiating Group wide contracts.
3. Economics, market and trading conditions
Group sales, expenses and operating results could vary 
significantly from period to period as a result of a variety 
of factors, some of which are outside the Group’s control. 
These factors include general economic conditions, 
conditions specific to the market and conditions specific 
to the Group. A negative change in economic conditions 
in the Group’s customer markets, including, for example, 
a downturn in the Canadian housing market, deterioration 
in consumer confidence or new products and processes 
entering the Group’s market place, could adversely impact 
the Group’s business. 
In addition, significant increases in energy costs, the cost of 
transport and distribution and employment costs in the 
locations where the Group’s manufacturing sites are based 
could adversely impact the profitability of the Group. 
Significant fluctuations in foreign currency exchange rates 
can have a material impact on the Group’s business, results 
of operations and overall financial position. The Group 
operates globally, with the majority of its revenues earned 
outside the UK and with significant investments around the 
world. As a result, the Group is subject to currency 
translation risk due to movements between various 
currencies (mainly the US Dollar and the Euro) and its 
reporting currency, Sterling. In order to reduce the effect of 
foreign exchange movements on its reported earnings, the 
Group borrows, where commercially appropriate, in the 
currencies of its operations, thus creating a natural hedge for 
a proportion of its balance sheet. The Group also enters into 
derivative financial instruments in currencies that partially 
hedge its net investment values. The Group does not 
undertake speculative treasury transactions.
As a result of the current economic uncertainties facing a 
number of countries around the world, there has been a 
change in the risk profile. An example is where credit 
insurance coverage has been withdrawn in certain countries. 
The outcome of the recent events remains uncertain.  
The austerity measures are likely to result in changes in 
growth rates and demand for products in those countries. 
These conditions may give rise to delays or defaults on 
contracts with customers based in countries experiencing 
difficulties and may affect the expectation of future business 
volumes and margins.
4. Financial covenants
The Group has financial covenants relating to its main source of 
long-term funding. This risk has materially reduced following the 
repayment of the debt facility following the disposal of the 
hygiene business. The Group expects to comply with these 
covenants. In the event that forecast profitability is not achieved, 
the continued need to comply with these covenants could 
restrict the operational flexibility and management decisions of 
the Group. There is also a risk that the Group’s long-term 
funding would need to be renegotiated with its debt-providers to 
ensure the continued operations of the Group and there could 
be no guarantee that such a renegotiation would be possible on 
commercially acceptable terms or that the Group would be able 
to successfully re-finance the relevant debt. 
Business Review continued
Financial Review continued 30    Fiberweb PLC  ANNUAL REPORT AND FINANCIAL STATEMENTS 2011 Fiberweb PLC  ANNUAL REPORT AND FINANCIAL STATEMENTS 2011    31  
The Group manages compliance with these covenants through 
careful monitoring of operating performance and cash flows, 
regular forecasts of future performance and tight management 
of capital expenditure. This risk has reduced following the 
repayment of the outstanding drawdowns under the Group RCF 
following the disposal of the Hygiene business.
5. Competition
The Group faces competition from global competitors that 
provide similar products to those offered by the Group. 
Competition in the industry is based upon: range and quality 
of products offered; the ability to deliver new products; 
geographical reach; reputation; price; and customer 
relationships. The hygiene market was characterised by large 
customers and some production over-capacity with the result 
that there is strong competition to secure contracts with these 
large customers. These risks are much less relevant to the 
continuing business. While these risks have not changed in 
nature over recent periods, prices and demand in the Group’s 
markets could be negatively affected if existing competitors 
increase their supply, or if new competitors enter the market 
with new products and/or favourable cost structures, or if 
important customers reduce demand or request significantly 
reduced prices. In response to a changing competitive 
environment, the Group may need from time to time to make 
certain pricing, service or marketing decisions that could have 
an adverse effect on its sales, results of operations and overall 
financial condition.
This risk is mitigated by the actions described at 2 above. 32    Fiberweb PLC  ANNUAL REPORT AND FINANCIAL STATEMENTS 2011
Business Review continued
Corporate Social Responsibility
Fiberweb endeavours to act in a socially responsible manner 
in all it does. Our businesses apply procedures appropriate 
to and compliant with local laws and operating conditions. 
In all our activities, we strive to ensure employee safety and 
we seek to protect the environment, public and occupational 
health and the communities within which we operate, while 
promoting profitability and business growth. Training and 
development opportunities and initiatives are provided to 
employees to develop and foster the skills, resources and 
knowledge they need to improve our business performance.
Policies and procedures have been established at group 
level which provide a guiding framework for our businesses 
to apply in conjunction with local practices. These include 
policies on ethical business practices, compliance with 
anti-trust laws, equal opportunities and anti-harassment and 
disability. Our market abuse and inside information policies 
govern behaviour in respect of share dealing, market abuse 
and dissemination of information to the market.
The manufacture of our products involves the use of large 
and complex manufacturing equipment and the Board 
attaches great importance to the safety and wellbeing of all 
our people. Matters relating to health and safety performance 
are reviewed and discussed at each Board meeting and as 
discussed below, we measure and track our employee safety 
record continuously.
Our businesses support the local communities in which they 
operate. Examples of some of the initiatives our people have 
been involved in during the year are discussed in more detail 
below. 
Employees
Fiberweb’s people are one of its most important 
resources. Their experience and expertise, their 
commitment to innovation and excellence and their drive 
to improve our performance is greatly valued.
 
Fiberweb’s policy is to provide equal opportunities for 
employment regardless of gender, race, colour, national 
origin, religion, age, marital status, sexual orientation 
or disability. Fiberweb takes compliance with anti- 
discrimination requirements very seriously in all the territories 
in which it operates. All our employees, both current 
and prospective, are given full and fair consideration for 
employment, training, career development and promotion, 
based on their skills and abilities. Fiberweb’s disability 
policy seeks to ensure that disabled people have the same 
opportunities as other employees for career development 
and training. Where premises, physical equipment and 
machinery or working methods could put a disabled job 
applicant or an employee at a disadvantage, Fiberweb will 
take all reasonable steps to overcome this. Any employee 
who becomes disabled whilst in employment will be given 
Fiberweb’s full support to ensure that they can continue in 
their existing job. Where this is not possible, retraining and 
redeployment for alternative vacancies will be considered.
Fiberweb believes in open communication channels across 
its businesses and employees are regularly provided with 
information concerning the performance and prospects of 
their local business unit and the global business. Internet 
based communications are used to provide information 
globally and employee councils and other local forums 
enable employees’ views to be heard and taken into 
account. In 2011 we launched a major management 
development programme – Fiberweb xL – to ensure that 
we both retain our most talented staff and prepare them for 
new and greater challenges within Fiberweb as their careers 
develop. This programme will continue in 2012 and the first 
cohort is due to complete the four module programme in 
June 2012. 
Health and Safety
Fiberweb remains committed to providing a safe and 
healthy workplace for its employees and visitors and to 
protecting the environment of the communities in which 
it operates. This commitment is a core business value 
and is integrated into our daily operations. w e continue 
to devote significant resources to our HS&e programme 
with the aim of achieving zero injuries and zero adverse 
environmental impacts while at the same time promoting 
profitability and business growth. 
 
HS&e Management System
Fiberweb is in the process of transforming its HS&E 
management system to follow the globally recognised 
International Standards Organisation (ISO) 14001 and the 
Occupational Health and Safety Assessment Series (OHSAS) 
18001 formats. These formats provide for a consistent and 
sustainable approach to managing HS&E globally. 
This transformation process began in 2010 with the 
development of the corporate HS&E management system 
elements, which establishes the framework and expectations 
for all operating facilities to follow. Whilst some operating 
facilities located in Europe currently have ISO 14001 and 
OHSAS 18001 certified management systems, the remaining 
facilities will begin developing site specific HS&E management 
systems, in accordance with the new corporate format.  32    Fiberweb PLC  ANNUAL REPORT AND FINANCIAL STATEMENTS 2011 Fiberweb PLC  ANNUAL REPORT AND FINANCIAL STATEMENTS 2011    33  
In 2011, a pilot implementation was successfully completed 
at the Green Bay facility in the US. The lessons learned 
from the pilot implementation will provide guidance and 
efficiencies across the organisation as the implementation 
process continues in the coming years. 
Fiberweb also maintains a three year HS&E strategy 
plan which outlines the key goals and strategies needed 
to sustain strong HS&E performance globally. Through 
periodic stakeholder review, this plan remains in alignment 
with our operations’ strategic plans, which promotes HS&E 
integration into our daily operations.
Compliance Assurance 
Fiberweb is committed to ensuring all operating facilities 
maintain strict compliance with HS&E regulations. T o that 
end, Fiberweb’s long standing compliance assurance 
programme has provided a comprehensive evaluation of 
conformance to applicable government regulations and 
corporate HS&E requirements. 
Once every three years, each operating facility participates 
in a comprehensive HS&E compliance audit. In addition, 
follow-up audits are performed to confirm any action items 
are completed as planned. In 2011, HS&E compliance audits 
were performed at facilities located in Biesheim, France; 
Norrköping, Sweden; T erno d’Isola, Italy; and Trezzano Rosa, 
Italy. Additionally, follow-up audits were performed at facilities 
in Gravatai, Brazil; San Jose Iturbide, Mexico; Simpsonville, 
South Carolina; Washougal, Washington; and Madison, 
T ennessee.
Since our HS&E compliance audits began in 2007, many 
audit findings have been identified to improve HS&E 
performance and conformance to regulatory requirements. 
Because each operating facility has taken responsibility to 
address these findings in a timely manner, the vast majority 
of all audit findings have been resolved.  
Global HSe Communications
We believe that regular communication is essential in 
sustaining an effective HS&E programme. Fiberweb 
therefore continues to conduct HS&E Lead T eam and HS&E 
Coordinator meetings which provide group-wide forums 
for sharing best practices, collaborating on continuous 
improvement initiatives and promoting the integration of 
HS&E into the overall business. In 2011, Fiberweb began 
communicating group-wide safety alerts and critical 
HS&E events to further enhance HS&E communication. 
Furthermore, the Americas and European HS&E 
Coordinators held routine conference calls throughout 2011 
to discuss HS&E programmes.
The following key elements provide an overview of our health 
and safety programmes and performance: 
1. Safety Performance Metrics 
Fiberweb uses two metrics globally to measure safety 
performance. The recordable injury rate (RIR) represents the 
number of recordable injuries per 100 full-time employees. 
The lost workday rate (LWDR) represents the number of 
injuries per 100 full-time employees, with one or more days 
away from work. In 2011, Fiberweb achieved a RIR of 1.7, 
which is 76% lower than the US industry average of 5.0. 
Further, 4 operating facilities completed the year without a 
single recordable injury and 7 operating facilities did not 
experience a single lost work day injury. Since 2001, our 
global recordable injury rate has been reduced by 53%.
The charts below compare Fiberweb’s global RIR and LWDR 
to the US industry averages. The industry average injury 
rates are obtained from the United States Department of 
Labor’s Bureau of Labor Statistics. Because the Bureau 
publishes injury rates at the end of each calendar year, 
the preceding year’s rates are used for the current year. 
Therefore, industry average injury rates reported for the 
current year will be updated the following year. 
 
 
Note: Statistics referenced in this report include Fiberweb 
and the FitesaFiberweb joint venture.
