2. Process Safety Management
Whilst Fiberweb facilities are not currently required to comply 
with the OSHA Process Safety Management (PSM) Standard, 
our manufacturing facilities continue to apply OSHA’s PSM 
principles to facilitate recognition and control of process 
hazards. T o ensure a comprehensive process analysis, 
Hazard and Operability (HAZOP) studies are performed by 
cross functional teams consisting of employees and HS&E 
professionals. In 2011, three follow-up HAZOP studies were 
performed, which brings the total number of HAZOP studies 
to over 30 since 2000. T o supplement the formal HAZOP 
process, Fiberweb facilities continue to use Process Safety 
Assessment tools to manage smaller scale changes to 
equipment and processes.  
3. Near Miss reporting
Fiberweb recognises that near miss reporting is a valuable 
leading safety performance indicator used in injury 
prevention. In recent years, modifications have been made 
to our electronic near miss reporting programme to promote 
reporting and ensure key information is available for analysis. 
T o that end, additional enhancements were made to the on-
line programme in 2011, which included a pilot study at two 
operating facilities. These enhancements to the programme 
are designed to streamline the reporting process, ensure 
critical data is captured and improve near miss trending and 
analysis. As a result of these efforts the number of near miss 
reports has doubled since 2009.  
4. resource exchange Process 
Fiberweb’s Resource Exchange Programme (REX) was 
developed in 2009 for the purpose of promoting professional 
development among HS&E Coordinators, evaluating HS&E 
compliance at operating facilities and sharing best practices 
across the Group. Following a structured schedule, REX 
participants visit Fiberweb operating facilities and interact 
with site leadership on HS&E topics. In 2011, all of the sites 
in the Americas (except the Brazil facility) and the sites in 
France and Sweden participated in the REX programme. 
5. “back to basics iii” (“b2b3”) Safety initiative
The “Back to Basics” safety initiative was developed by 
Fiberweb in 2007. The initiative was developed for the purpose 
of promoting awareness of historical safety and providing 
another system for identifying hazards at operating locations. 
The initiative has undergone three revisions and remains to be 
a key injury prevention tool in Fiberweb’s HS&E programme. 
Awards and recognition
Our facility in Green Bay, US, continues to represent an 
exemplary HS&E programme. Along with maintaining 
OSHA’s VPP STAR status, the facility volunteered to pilot the 
implementation of Fiberweb’s recently developed HS&E 
management system. Over the course of six months, the site 
developed the management system elements, completed 
the key requirements in accordance with ISO 14001 and 
OHSAS 18001 and conducted employee training sessions.  
In addition, the facility continued its safety performance 
record of operating for over 9 years without a recordable 
injury and for over 14 years without a lost workday injury.
The Environment
Fiberweb is committed to developing and promoting 
products and processes that reduce waste and adverse 
environmental impacts. This includes both the efficient 
use of materials and energy in product design and 
development and an awareness of the effect on the 
environment of our manufacturing processes and end 
use of our products.
 
Fiberweb encourages each of its facilities to develop its own 
environmental programmes and to work towards reducing 
its environmental impact. We continue to focus on identifying 
and improving performance in key areas of environmental 
impact, which include waste reduction, energy consumption, 
water consumption, the use of recycled and biodegradable 
materials and packaging.
Our businesses are encouraged to report all environmental 
impacts and key performance information which is collected 
twice a year through the Environmental Index Reporting 
System, an electronic data collection system. The data is 
collated annually and provides a means by which our 
businesses can evaluate their environmental performance  
and set improvement targets. In 2011, several additional  
key environmental performance indicators (KPIs) were added 
to the Environmental Index, including new fuel usage 
categories, water discharge, environmental management  
and information regarding community and social programmes. 
Fiberweb continues to focus on identifying and improving 
performance in key areas of environmental impact, which 
include energy consumption. FitesaFiberweb has formed an 
Energy Committee which consists of a Coordinator, a 
Sponsor and a member from each FitesaFiberweb facility.  34    Fiberweb PLC  ANNUAL REPORT AND FINANCIAL STATEMENTS 2011 Fiberweb PLC  ANNUAL REPORT AND FINANCIAL STATEMENTS 2011    35  
The goal of the Energy Committee is to reduce the amount of 
energy FitesaFiberweb uses to produce its products through 
the sharing of best practices, trending of key performance 
indicators and a drive for continuous improvement. Its facility 
in Washougal started a High Performance Utility 
Management (HPUM) project with its energy provider.  
T o date, this project has saved approximately 700,000 kWh 
of energy since 1 July 2010 compared to the previous year. 
At the facility in Abedare, UK, the extrusion of biopolymers to 
manufacture tree shelters uses 10% less energy than using 
only polypropylene. This is due to the reduced process 
temperatures and lower melt viscosity of the biopolymer 
material. 
At our facility in Old Hickory, US an inefficient coal-fired 
steam plant has been replaced with a state-of the-art natural 
gas-fired central utilities plant. Previously, Old Hickory 
received its electricity from a neighbouring coal-fired facility. 
The new plant produces significantly less carbon dioxide, 
nitrogen oxides and sulphur dioxide, while enabling the plant 
to continuously operate – even in the event of plant failure.
Social and Community Matters 
Fiberweb’s businesses are encouraged to become involved 
with their local communities through a range of organisations 
and initiatives. Examples of the support given in 2011 are:
• In our US operations, our employees continue to support 
their local communities in a variety of ways including 
the donation of equipment and voluntary work for local 
schools and organisations. 
• United Way is a nationally recognised, community-based 
organisation in the US that provides local funding to a 
large number of smaller charities and community services 
and is the officially designated charitable organisation that 
Fiberweb sponsors in the US for employee contributions. 
This support is provided through employee donations.
• The Simpsonville facility and its employees have provided 
financial and other support to a number of local voluntary 
organisations and charities including United Way, blood 
drives and food donations.
• Fiberweb Sweden sponsors an association against drugs 
and also participates in a class at a local high school 
which involves visits and participation in practical work 
projects.
Sustainability and the Supply Chain
Fiberweb continues to work actively to design and develop 
products that promote sustainable development principles 
and do not adversely impact the environment or the health 
and safety of the communities it serves. This is pursued 
primarily through our R&D innovation strategy as well 
as centralised procurement or, where this is impractical, 
local sourcing. Sustainability plays an important role in 
our research and development activities where we seek 
to develop ways to reduce raw material usage and energy 
consumption and work with customers and suppliers to 
develop products with improved sustainability.
We actively seek to develop and market products which use 
renewable and recycled materials and we participate in a 
number of sustainability-related initiatives of our 
stakeholders, including our suppliers and investor groups.  
In 2011, we formed a Sustainability Steering Committee to 
develop our sustainability strategy and objectives and to 
monitor and report on our performance in this area.  
We expect to be in a position to issue our first Sustainability 
Report highlighting our strategy, objectives and performance 
around the middle of 2012. 36    Fiberweb PLC  ANNUAL REPORT AND FINANCIAL STATEMENTS 2011

Principal Activities and business review
Fiberweb is an international group of businesses involved in the 
development, manufacturing and supply of specialist industrial 
and construction materials. It operates principally in Europe and 
North America and has a strong portfolio of products and brands 
and market leading positions in several countries.
Fiberweb plc is the Group holding company. The subsidiary and 
associated undertakings principally affecting the profits and net 
assets of the Group in the year are listed on page 100.
The Company is required to set out in this report a Business 
Review and a Corporate Governance Statement. The Business 
Review is the “Management Report” for the purpose of DTR 
4.1.8R. This report and the Business Review set out a fair review 
of the business of the Group during the financial year ended  
31 December 2011, including an analysis of the position of the 
Group at the end of the financial year and a description of the 
principal risks and uncertainties facing the Group.
The information that fulfils the requirements of the Business 
Review are set out on pages 10 to 35 and comprise:

results and Dividends
The continuing underlying loss before taxation of the Group was 
£(5.1) million (2010: £6.1 million profit). The full results for the year, 
which were approved by the Board of Directors on 29 February 
2012, are set out in the accompanying financial statements and 
the notes thereto on pages 55 to 103.
An interim dividend of 1.0 pence per share was paid on 4 
November 2011. The Directors recommend the payment of a final 
dividend for 2011 of 2.0 pence per share (2010: 2.5 pence per 
share), making a total dividend for the year of 3.0 pence per share 
(2010: 4.2 pence per share). Subject to shareholder approval, the 
final dividend will be payable on 25 May 2012 to shareholders on 
the register at the close of business on 27 April 2012. A dividend 
reinvestment plan (“DRIP”) is in place that allows shareholders 
to purchase additional shares in the Company using their cash 
dividend. Further information regarding the plan is set out in 
Shareholder Information on page 105.
Acquisitions and Disposals
The Group acquired the entire issued share capital of Boddingtons 
International Limited, the parent company of the Boddingtons 
group of companies, a leading UK based specialist geosynthetic 
and accessory manufacturer, for a consideration comprising £8.2 
million and the assumption of debt of £0.9 million. The acquisition 
was completed on 6 January 2011 and the consideration of 
£8.2 million was satisfied by a payment of £4.5 million in cash 
and the issue of 4.5 million new ordinary Fiberweb plc shares, 
representing approximately 3.5% of Fiberweb’s enlarged issued 
share capital. Boddingtons has been integrated into the Group’s 
Geosynthetics segment.
The Group acquired the entire issued share capital of Tubex 
Limited, the parent company of the Tubex group of companies, 
the largest European specialist producer of tree shelters, for a 
consideration comprising £5.1 million and the assumption of debt 
of £0.7 million. The acquisition was completed on 17 May 2011 
and the total consideration was satisfied by a payment of £3.85 
million in cash and the issue of 1.8 million new ordinary Fiberweb 
plc shares, representing approximately 1.05% of Fiberweb’s 
enlarged issued share capital. Tubex has been integrated into the 
Group’s Geosynthetics segment.
The Group disposed of the majority of its hygiene business 
to Petropar S.A. for a total consideration of US$286 million 
(approximately £184 million). The disposal was completed on 
30 December 2011 and the total consideration was satisfied 
by the payment of US$260 million in cash and the issue of a 
US$26 million Vendor Loan Note payable by Petropar S.A. by  
30 December 2012 and attracting a 6% interest rate. The sale  
has allowed Fiberweb to become a focused leader in certain 
attractive segments of the growing technical fabrics and construction 
products markets, with leading positions in several attractive 
market and technology niches, notably in filtration, construction 
specialties, geosynthetics, agriculture and several medical areas. 
The disposal enabled the Group to repay all of the amounts owed 
under the Revolving Credit Facility on 5 January 2012.
Capital Structure
Details of the authorised and issued share capital of the Company, 
including movements during the year and the number of shares 
in issue at the end of the year, are shown in note 26 on page 91. 
The Company has one class of ordinary shares which carries 
no right to fixed income and each share carries the right to one 
vote at general meetings of the Company. The rights attaching 
to the ordinary shares are defined in the Company’s Articles of 
Association. All issued shares are fully paid.
There are no specific restrictions on the transfer of shares, the 
size of a holding or voting rights, which are all matters governed 
by the Articles of Association. The Directors are not aware of any 
agreements between holders of the Company’s shares that may 
result in restrictions on the transfer of securities or on voting rights. 
No person has any special rights of control over the Company’s 
share capital, so far as the Directors are aware.
Details of the significant holdings of ordinary shares as notified to 
the Company are shown in the table of Substantial Shareholdings  
and Voting Rights on page 39. No shares are held by the Fiberweb 
Employee Benefit Trust. Details of employee share schemes are 
set out in note 25 on page 90.

Going Concern
The Group’s business activities, together with the factors likely 
to affect its future development, performance and position are 
set out in the Business Review on pages 10 to 35. The financial 
position of the Group, its cash flows, liquidity position and 
borrowing facilities are described in the Financial Review on 
pages 23 to 31. In addition, notes 20 and 21 to the Consolidated 
Financial Statements include the Group’s objectives, policies and 
processes for managing its capital, its financial risk management 
objectives, details of its financial instruments and hedging 
activities and its exposures to liquidity risk. Credit risk exposure is 
discussed in note 16 on page 77.
At 31 December 2011, the Group had net cash of £22 million 
(2010: net debt of £151.2 million). Following the disposal of the 
majority of the hygiene business in December 2011, the Group 
amended its existing revolving credit loan facility (“RCF”) provided 
by a syndicate of several international banks. The amended RCF 
has a remaining term of one and a half years until July 2013 and 
comprises a €30 million and $40 million multi-currency facility. The 
RCF is subject to the financial covenants set out on pages 80 to 
82 in note 20. At 31 December 2011, £157.8 million (2010: £173.7 
million) was drawn down under the RCF prior to the amendment 
discussed above and was repaid on 5 January 2012 using the 
proceeds of the disposal of the hygiene business.
The Group prepares regular business forecasts and monitors its 
projected compliance with its banking covenants under the RCF, 
which is reviewed by the Board. Forecasts are then adjusted 
for sensitivities which address the principal risks to which the 
Group is exposed, such as fluctuations in raw material prices, 
exchange rates and best estimates of the possible impact of the 
macroeconomic environment on the Group’s underlying trading 
results. Consideration is then given to the potential actions 
available to management to mitigate the impact of one or more 
of the sensitivities. The Group’s central and sensitised forecasts, 
after applying reasonable possible adverse variations in trading 
performance, show that the Group is able to operate within the 
level of the RCF and remain covenant compliant. Covenant tests 
are required quarterly under the RCF.
After making enquires, the Directors have a reasonable expectation 
that the Company and the Group have adequate resources 
to continue in operational existence for the foreseeable future. 
Accordingly, they continue to adopt the going concern basis in 
preparing the annual report and financial statements.
Charitable and Political Donations
The Company made no political donations during the year. Group 
donations to charities worldwide were £16,273 (2010: £48,640), 
with UK charities receiving £1,500 (2010: £10,000). Charitable 
donations comprise amounts paid in support of local community 
initiatives and charities. No charitable donations were individually 
material.
Supplier Payment Policy
It is the Company’s and Group’s policy to negotiate terms of 
payment with suppliers when agreeing the terms of each 
transaction to ensure that the terms of payment are clearly 
understood and it is the Company’s policy to abide by terms of 
payment. Trade creditors of the Group at 31 December 2011  
were equivalent to 52 days’ purchases (2010: 50 days) based on 
the average daily amount invoiced by suppliers during the year.

Directors’ indemnities
The Company entered into a Deed of Indemnity with each Director 
of the Company upon their appointment and each Deed of 
Indemnity remains in force at the date of this report. The terms 
of each of these deeds are identical and reflect the statutory 
provisions on indemnities introduced by the Companies (Audit, 
Investigations and Community Enterprise) Act 2004. Under the 
terms of each deed, the Company undertakes to indemnify the 
relevant Director, to the fullest extent permitted by law, against any 
and all liability, howsoever caused (including by that Director’s 
own negligence), suffered or incurred by that Director in the 
course of acting as a Director or employee of the Company or any 
member of the Group.

in favour of the Company Secretary and persons discharging 
managerial responsibility on 30 October 2006. The terms of 
the Deed Poll are similar to the terms of the Deed of Indemnity 
entered into with the Directors.
The Deeds of Indemnity, Deed Poll of Indemnity and the Company’s 
Articles of Association are available for inspection during normal 
business hours at the Company’s registered office and will also be 
available for inspection at the Annual General Meeting.

Corporate Governance
Fiberweb plc is committed to complying with the best practice 
principles of the UK Corporate Governance Code adopted 
by the Financial Reporting Council in May 2010 (the “Code”). 
The Company considers that it has, during the year ended 
31 December 2011, complied in full with the provisions of the 
Code, except in respect of Code provision A.4.1, as independent 
Non-Executive Directors do not form a majority of the members 
of the Nomination Committee. Details and explanations of the 
application of the Code are given later in this report.
Incorporated in this report by reference are details of significant 
holdings of and special rights of control over the Company’s 
share capital, voting rights, rules relating to the appointment 
and replacement and powers of Directors and amendment of 
the Articles of Association of the Company which are set out on  
pages 38 and 39. A going concern statement can be found on 
page 39. The business model and strategy for delivering the 
objectives of the Company are set out on pages 10 to 14.
The role of the board
The Board as a whole has responsibility for the success of the 
Company. The Board meets regularly to determine the strategic 
direction of the Group and to review operating, financial and risk 
performance. Specific responsibilities are delegated to Board 
Committees as described later in this report.
There is a formal schedule of matters reserved for the Board that 
includes approval of the following:
q 	 the Group’s long term objectives and strategy;
q 	 	 acquisitions, disposals and capital expenditure projects above 
certain thresholds;
q 	 	all guarantees and treasury related transactions above certain 
thresholds;
q 	 	the financial statements and assessment of financial 
performance;
q 	 the Company’s dividend policy;
q 	 	transactions involving the issue or purchase of Company 
shares;
q 	 the Group’s risk management strategy;
q 	 	legal actions brought by or against the Group above certain 
thresholds;
q 	 	appointments to the Board and the appointment of the 
Company Secretary;
q 	 	 Group policies and the scope of delegations by the Board; and
q 	 Committees and executive management of the Group.
The full schedule of matters reserved for the Board can be viewed 
on the Company’s website at www.fiberweb.com. The schedule of 
matters is reviewed on an annual basis. Matters outside the scope 
of the formal schedule of matters are decided by management 
in accordance with the delegated authority limits set out in the 
Group Authority and Signing Policy.
In order to ensure that all matters are given due consideration, 
the Board has adopted a schedule of agenda items, which is 
reviewed and updated annually. These agenda items include:
q 	 an annual strategy review;
q 	 divisional updates and business plans;
q 	 annual budget setting and approval;
q 	 a review of Group policies; and
q 	 succession planning.
At each meeting, the Board receives information from the 
Chief Executive Officer and the Chief Financial Officer on the 
performance and results of the Group and individual operating 
businesses, the Group’s current financial position and updates on 
any other significant matters. The Divisional Managing Directors 
and Heads of Functions present to the Board from time to time 
and other senior managers and the Company Secretary update 
the Board on developments in their area of responsibility.
The Directors are generally provided with detailed and 
comprehensive papers in advance of each Board meeting. The 
agenda is set by the Chairman in conjunction with the Chief 
Executive Officer, the Chief Financial Officer and the Company 
Secretary. The Company Secretary is responsible to the Board 
for the timeliness and quality of information and is responsible for 
advising the Board on corporate governance matters and Board 
procedures. All Directors have access to the advice and services 
of the Company Secretary.
The Company Secretary acts as secretary to all Board Committees. 
The Directors may take independent professional advice at the 
Company’s expense in relation to their responsibilities as directors. 
None of the Directors obtained independent professional advice 
in this regard in the period under review.
The number of Board and Board Committee meetings held during 
the year and individual attendance by the Directors at those 
meetings are set out in the table below.
Malcolm Coster, Daniel Dayan and Daniel Abrams all attended 
meetings of the Audit Committee and Remuneration Committee 
at the invitation of the Chairmen of those Committees.

met formally without the Executive Directors on at least one 
occasion and held several informal discussions without the

The board, board balance and independence
The Board comprises two Executive Directors and four Non-
Executive Directors (including the Chairman) who contribute a 
wide range of complementary skills and experience. Details of 
each director’s skills and experience are set out on pages 36 
and 37.
The Chairman of the Board is Malcolm Coster. The Chairman’s 
other significant commitments are set out on page 37.
The Chief Executive Officer is Daniel Dayan. Richard Stillwell is 
the Senior Independent Director. He is available to shareholders if 
they have concerns that the normal channels of contact with the 
Chairman or Chief Executive Officer would not resolve.
The Board believes that there is an appropriate balance of 
executive and Non-Executive Directors on the Board, without 
one individual or group dominating the Board’s decision-making 
process.
The Board has determined all its Non-Executive Directors to be 
independent in character and judgement. This includes Richard 
Stillwell who served as a non-executive director of BBA Group plc, 
the company from which the Company demerged in 2006.  
The Board considers Richard Stillwell to be independent 
notwithstanding his prior service with BBA Group plc. The Non- 
Executive Chairman, Malcolm Coster, was considered 
independent in character and judgement on appointment. The 
Board will assess the independence of its Non-Executive Directors 
on a continuous basis.
Following the introduction on 1 October 2008 of the statutory 
duty of directors to avoid situations which have or may have an 
interest which conflicts or possibly may conflict with the interests 
of the Company, the Nomination Committee has been given 
responsibility for considering and if appropriate authorising such 
conflict situations on such terms as are considered necessary or 
if material referring them to the Board, on an ongoing basis. Any 
director in a conflicting or potentially conflicting situation is excluded 
from any decision. During the year the Nomination Committee 
reviewed the conflict situations authorised and concluded that they 
remained appropriate and accordingly the Company has complied 
with the procedures in place to ensure the effective operation of 
the Board’s powers to authorise conflict situations.
role of the Chairman and Chief executive Officer
The roles of Chairman and Chief Executive Officer are separate 
and there is a clear division of responsibilities between these 
roles. In accordance with the Code, the Board has adopted a 
formal written statement of the division of responsibilities between 
the Chairman and the Chief Executive Officer.
The Chairman leads the Board and ensures the effective 
engagement and contribution of all Non-Executive and Executive 
Directors. In conjunction with the Company Secretary, he is 
responsible for ensuring that directors receive information in an 
accurate, clear and timely manner and for promoting effective 
decision making. He is also responsible for ensuring that directors 
continually update their skills and knowledge. The Chairman has 
active contact and involvement with the Executive Directors and 
the affairs of the Company. This serves to keep him abreast of 
current business issues but also provides the Executive Directors 
with access to an independent opinion on day to day business 
decisions.
The Chief Executive Officer has responsibility for the day to day 
management of the Group’s businesses and acts in accordance 
with the authority delegated by the Board. He is responsible 
for developing and proposing a strategy for consideration 
and adoption by the Board and for implementing the Board’s 
strategies, decisions and policies. He is also responsible for 
ensuring that the business strategy and activities are effectively 
communicated and promoted within and outside the business,  
for building positive relationships with the Company’s stakeholders 
and for creating and developing the Company’s culture.
board Appointments
Primary responsibility for planned and progressive refreshing of 
the Board lies with the Board. The Board, through the work of the 
Nomination Committee, ensures that there is a formal, rigorous 
and transparent procedure for the appointment of new directors. 
Further details of the work of the Nomination Committee are set 
out on page 45.
Appointments of Non-Executive Directors are made by the Board 
for an initial term of three years, subject to the usual regulatory 
provisions and continued satisfactory performance of their duties. 
Re-appointment for a further term is not automatic but may be 
made by mutual agreement.
In accordance with the Company’s Articles of Association, all 
directors are subject to re-election by shareholders at least every 
three years.
On appointment, all Non-Executive Directors are advised of the 
time commitment expected of them to fulfil their duties. Letters 
of appointment for the Non-Executive Directors are available for 
inspection on request.
board induction and Professional Development
The Board has adopted a formal written programme for the 
induction of new directors to familiarise themselves with the 
Group’s businesses, understand the goals, objectives and 
mission of the Company and develop an awareness and 
understanding of the views of the Company’s major shareholders. 
The programme is also structured to enable new directors to  
gain an understanding of their own specific duties and 
responsibilities. The programme, developed in accordance with 
the Institute of Chartered Secretaries and Administrators  
guidelines on Board induction, is made up of a combination of 
selected written corporate information, meetings with key senior 
management and site visits and is tailored to take account of  
each new director’s specific needs, skills and experience. Where 
a non-executive director is also being appointed as a member of 
one of the Board Committees, his or her induction will cover 
matters such as the role of and terms of reference of the relevant 
Committee.
In order to maintain, develop and update each director’s knowledge 
and capabilities, the Board and its Committees are briefed on 
corporate governance and regulatory developments as they arise. 
The Audit Committee is briefed on technical and accounting 
matters as a matter of routine at each meeting by senior 
management and the external auditors. The directors receive 
information and training in respect of their statutory duties and their 
disclosure obligations under the Disclosure and Transparency 
Rules and the Listing Rules. A continuous programme of 
development will occur as required.
The Board regards performance evaluation as an important part 
of monitoring and improving its effectiveness and a formal internal 
appraisal of the Board, the Board Committees and the individual 
directors was undertaken during the year. This involved the 
Chairman, acting on behalf of the Board, obtaining views from and 
evaluating the performance of the Board, the Board Committees 
and the individual directors and the Non-Executive Directors, led 
by the Senior Independent Director, assessing the performance 
of the Chairman. An internal evaluation was considered by the 
Board to be adequate given the size and current position and 
circumstances of the Company and accordingly the evaluation 
was not externally facilitated.

Audit Committee
The Audit Committee consists of three independent, Non-Executive 
Directors and is chaired by Stephen Dryden. Its other members are 
Richard Stillwell and Brian Taylorson. Both Stephen Dryden and 
Brian Taylorson are qualified Chartered Accountants and currently 
hold senior finance roles in major UK listed public companies.
The terms of reference of the Audit Committee include all 
matters listed in Code provision C.3.2 although in practice risk 
management is reviewed by the Board as a whole. The terms of 
reference are reviewed annually and any proposed revisions are 
formally approved and adopted by the Board.
The Audit Committee is responsible for making recommendations 
to the Board on the appointment of the external auditors and 
their remuneration. The Committee reviews the external auditors’ 
independence and considers the nature, scope and results of the 
auditors’ work and the provision of non-audit services by them. 
The Committee focuses particularly on compliance with legal and 
other regulatory requirements, accounting standards and ensuring 
that an effective system of internal controls is maintained. The 
Committee may consider any financial matter that may have an 
impact on the Company. The ultimate responsibility for reviewing 
and approving the annual and interim financial statements and 
bi-annual trading statements remains with the Board.
The Audit Committee normally meets not less than three times a year 
at dates to coincide with the financial reporting cycle. The Committee 
also meets privately with the external auditors and the internal 
auditors at least once a year. The Chairman may call a meeting at 
the request of the Executive Directors or the external auditors.
In addition to Committee members, the Chairman of the Board, 
the Chief Executive Officer, the Chief Financial Officer, the Group 
Financial Controller, the internal auditor and the external auditors 
normally attend meetings at the invitation of the Committee Chairman.
During the year and up to the date of this report, the Audit 
Committee considered the following matters and took the 
following actions in the discharge of its duties:
q 	 	reviewed and advised the Board on the financial statements in 
the 2010 report and accounts;
q 	 	reviewed and assessed the audit services provided and the 
effectiveness of the external auditors;
q 	 	discussed and agreed the nature and the scope of work to be 
performed by the external auditors;
q 	 	reviewed the effectiveness of the Group’s internal control 
systems established by management and reviewed the 
Board’s sign-off procedure on the system of internal controls, 
which are set out in more detail on page 44;
q 	 	reviewed the scope of the work and effectiveness of the 
internal audit function and the manner in which internal audit 
services will be provided;
q 	 	received and reviewed reports from the internal audit function 
on the work undertaken during the year;
q 	 	reviewed the policy on the provision of non-audit services by 
the external auditors and assessed the independence of the 
auditors; and
q 	 	reviewed the arrangements by which concerns can be raised 
by staff in respect of possible matters of financial impropriety 
or other matters.
Auditor independence and effectiveness
The external auditors were appointed in 2006. One of the key 
responsibilities of the Committee is to ensure that the independence 
and objectivity of the external auditors is safeguarded. The 
Committee has adopted a policy on the provision of non-audit 
services that is in line with the Accounting Practice Board’s 
Ethical Standards. This policy is reviewed annually. It prohibits the 
external auditors from providing certain additional services to the 
Group such as bookkeeping, internal audit, valuations, actuarial 
services and financial systems design and implementation. The 
external auditors are, however, permitted to provide assurance 
services such as reporting accountant work, due diligence and 
certain tax services.
The Group’s general policy is not to use the external auditors for 
acquisition and due diligence work. However, where the Group 
considers it appropriate or conflicts arise, suppliers other than the 
preferred supplier may be asked to tender and this may include 
the external auditors. In accordance with the policy, the Chairman 
of the Committee or, in his absence, another designated member 
of the Committee is required to pre-approve certain permitted 
services that exceed the financial limits set out in the policy. For 
non-audit tax fees, the annual pre-approval limit is set at £200,000 
and the pre-approval limit for any one project is set at £100,000. 
For all other services, the pre-approval limit for any one project is 
set at £50,000. The Audit Committee reviews these limits at least 
annually.
A summary of the overall level of non-audit fees paid to the 
external auditors is presented at each Audit Committee meeting. 
Details of the amounts paid to the external auditors, Deloitte LLP, 
for audit and non-audit services provided during the year are 
given in note 4 on page 68.
During the year, the external auditors provided reporting 
accountant services in relation to the rights issue undertaken 
in the first half of the year and reporting accountant and due 
diligence services in relation to the disposal of a majority of the 
Group’s Hygiene business completed in the second half of the 
year. The Audit Committee reviewed the nature and cost of this 
work during the year and approved the ongoing involvement of 
Deloitte LLP in this regard as it was concluded that they were best 
placed to supply such services in a cost effective manner due 
to the experience and qualifications of the individuals providing 
such services and their knowledge of the Group and that the 
best interests of the Group were served by engaging them.  
The Audit Committee reviewed the nature and cost of the non-
audit work undertaken during the year and the safeguards Deloitte 
had in place to protect their independence as auditors and was 
satisfied that this work has not impaired their independence as 
external auditors.
To fulfil its responsibility regarding the independence of the 
external auditors, the Audit Committee has during the year:
q 	 	reviewed the independence of the external auditors and the 
arrangements Deloitte LLP have in place to identify, report and 
manage conflicts of interest;
q 	 	considered the effectiveness of the external auditors through 
a review of their plan of work and the outputs arising from the 
audit; and
q 	 	 considered the overall extent of non-audit services provided by 
the external auditors, in addition to case by case approval of 
the provision of non-audit services as appropriate as set out 
above. As a result of the above, and taking into account the tenure of 
the auditors, the Committee concluded the independence criteria 
under the relevant standards continue to be met and that it was 
not necessary to tender for the audit work. Accordingly, the 
Committee recommended to the Board the re-appointment of 
Deloitte LLP as external auditors.
internal Control and risk Management
The Board has overall responsibility for the Group’s system of 
internal control and risk management and reviews its effectiveness 
on an annual basis.
The implementation and maintenance of risk management is 
the responsibility of the Executive Directors and other senior 
management and a system has been established to identify, 
evaluate and manage the significant risks that the Group faces. 
The system is designed to mitigate rather than eliminate altogether 
the risk of failure to achieve business objectives and can only 
provide reasonable and not absolute assurance against material 
misstatement or loss.
The main elements of the Group’s internal control system are as 
follows:
1.  The Board
The Board has overall responsibility for the Group’s system of 
internal control. As mentioned above in this report, the Board 
meets regularly and has a schedule of matters reserved for its 
approval and the Board Committees operate within their terms 
of reference. This structure includes the Audit Committee which, 
with the Chief Financial Officer, reviews the effectiveness of the 
internal financial and operating control environment of the Group. 
All acquisitions and disposals of companies or businesses are 
approved by the Board.
2.  Strategic and Business Planning
The Group and each business unit produce and agree a business 
plan each year against which the performance of the business is 
regularly monitored.
3.  Monthly Management Accounts
Detailed monthly management accounts that measure actual 
performance against budget are submitted by management.  
A monthly report is provided to the Board, highlighting key issues 
and summarising the detailed financial information provided by 
the operating units. Forecasts of sales, profits and operating cash 
are reviewed at least quarterly and presented to the Board.
4.  Internal Audit
PricewaterhouseCoopers LLP as the internal auditor undertakes 
a programme of reviews aligned to the business risks. The Audit 
Committee receives a report from the internal auditor at each 
meeting that includes the findings of the reviews conducted and 
any actions agreed with management to be undertaken to improve 
the effectiveness of controls. The internal auditor has direct access 
to the Chairman of the Audit Committee. The Audit Committee 
reviews the effectiveness of the internal audit activities, including 
the scope of work, authority and resources of the internal auditor 
and reviews the internal audit plan at least annually.
5.  System of Control Procedures and Delegated Authorities 
There are clearly defined guidelines and approval limits for capital 
and operating expenditure and other key business transactions 
and decisions that have been approved by the Board. A detailed 
matrix defines the levels of authority for the Group’s senior 
management and their direct reports including in relation to 
acquisitions, capital expenditure, commercial and employee 
contracts and treasury matters.
6.  Treasury Policies and Procedures
Detailed procedures exist for investments, currency and 
commodity hedging, the granting of guarantees and the use of 
treasury products.
7.  Risk Identification, Monitoring and Management Procedures 
A process is in place to collate schedules of risks for each key 
site, which are then reviewed by the Divisional Managing Directors 
and consolidated into a schedule of the significant divisional 
level risks. Risks identified cover business, financial, compliance, 
operational as well as environmental, social and governance 
risks. These risk schedules, which include an assessment of their 
likelihood and impact, are kept under review and are presented 
for review at least annually at a Fiberweb Executive Team meeting. 
The Fiberweb Executive Team is responsible for confirming that 
the plans to mitigate those risks are satisfactory and for improving 
internal controls and processes. The Chief Financial Officer is 
responsible for reporting the work of the Fiberweb Executive Team 
on risk management to the Board.
8.  Organisational Structure
Structures are in place at the Company’s Head Office and at 
divisional level that clearly define responsibilities for operational, 
accounting, taxation, treasury, legal, company secretarial and 
insurance functions.
9.  Financial Control and Reporting
The Group has adopted policies that are appropriate and as such,  
it has a full set of accounting policies and procedures in force. 
These are regularly reviewed for appropriateness and, when 
required, updated accordingly. Senior management of each 
business are asked to sign an annual confirmation that their 
business has complied with the Group Accounting Policies manual 
in the preparation of the consolidated financial statements.
The Fiberweb Group uses Hyperion Financial Management 
(“HFM”) for the consolidation of both monthly management 
accounts and annual and interim accounts. Results are prepared 
in accordance with IFRS. Businesses upload individual entity 
results into HFM via a secure internet link. Entity results are 
extracted from local ERP systems in trial balance format which  
are mapped to the common HFM chart of accounts. Entity results 
are reviewed by entity and divisional management prior to 
submission to HFM. The results are consolidated within HFM.  
HFM contains a number of validation checks and controls to 
ensure the accuracy of financial information. Results are reviewed 
by senior management including the Fiberweb Executive Team 
and the Board.
10. Group Policies
A new Group Policy Manual was adopted in 2007 and 
communicated to all businesses. The policies are reviewed 
regularly and revised as necessary to take account of changing 
law and circumstances. New policies are added when appropriate. 
A review of compliance with a number of these policies by 
Group companies has been introduced and the results are 
communicated to the Fiberweb Executive Team and the Board 
as necessary.
44     Fiberweb PLC  ANNUAL REPORT AND FINANCIAL STATEMENTS 2011
Corporate Governance continued Fiberweb PLC  ANNUAL REPORT AND FINANCIAL STATEMENTS 2011    45  
11. Health, Safety and Environmental Manual (HS&E)
A Group Health, Safety and Environmental Manual details policies, 
standards and procedures that are applicable throughout the 
Group. Further information is included in the Business Review on 
pages 32 to 34. A monthly report is prepared and circulated to 
the Fiberweb Executive Team on HS&E matters and the Board 
receives a report on HS&E matters at each Board meeting.
The Board confirms that there is an ongoing process for 
identifying, evaluating and managing the significant risks faced by 
the Group and that it has been in place for the period under review 
up to the date of approval of the annual report and accounts.  
The Group’s system is reviewed by the Board and accords with 
the Turnbull guidance. Any significant failings or weaknesses that 
come to management’s and the Board’s attention are addressed 
and appropriate action taken.
The Company had board representation in the FitesaFiberweb 
joint venture and, whilst not applied in their entirety, a number of 
Group policies were adopted by the joint venture. The joint venture 
was subject to the Company’s internal audit procedures and for 
management reporting purposes the joint venture was integrated 
with the Company. The financial results were separately audited 
but were reviewed by the Company’s external auditors.
Nomination Committee
The Nomination Committee is chaired by Malcolm Coster and its 
other members are Daniel Dayan, Richard Stillwell and Stephen 
Dryden. Whilst the Committee leads the process for Board 
appointments, the Chairman will consult with all the directors on 
a regular basis throughout the process. While the composition of 
the Nomination Committee is not in compliance with A.4.1 of the 
Code, in the opinion of the Board it provides a suitable balance of 
knowledge and experience and the constitution of the Committee is 
appropriate given the size of the Board and the process undertaken 
for Board appointments. The Chairman will not participate in any 
discussion relating to the appointment of his successor.
The Committee has responsibility for identifying and nominating 
candidates for Board vacancies and making recommendations 
to the Board in relation to the appointment of the Company’s 
executive and Non-Executive Directors. Before making an 
appointment, the Committee will evaluate the balance of skills, 
knowledge and experience on the Board and, in light of this 
evaluation, prepare a description of the role and capabilities 
required for a particular appointment. Use will be made of 
external recruitment consultants and the final decision regarding 
appointment rests with the Board. The Committee also has 
responsibility for reviewing and if appropriate authorising conflicts 
of interest or potential conflicts of interest of directors.
One Nomination Committee meeting was held during the year at 
which the re-election of Daniel Abrams and Richard Stillwell as 
directors of the Company was considered and recommended to 
the Board for approval and at which potential conflicts of interest 
were reviewed and considered.
Shareholder relations
The Board as a whole is kept up to date on the views of 
Fiberweb’s major shareholders. This is achieved through regular 
meetings during the year between the Chief Executive Officer, the 
Chief Financial Officer and major shareholders to discuss matters 
of mutual interest that are reported to the Board. Broker reports 
are routinely circulated to the Board.
The Chairman and the Senior Independent Director also met 
with major shareholders during the year. The Board considers 
that the Chairman and the Senior Independent Director 
have an understanding and awareness of the issues and 
concerns of major shareholders and the Chairman, the Senior 
Independent Director and the other Non-Executive Directors  
were available to meet shareholders at the Annual General Meeting.
Both institutional and private shareholders are welcome at the 
Annual General Meeting. The meeting provides an opportunity 
for shareholders to discuss with executive and Non-Executive 
Directors any issues concerning the Company and its activities. 
The Chairman of the Board and the Chairmen of the Audit, 
Remuneration and Nomination Committees are available to 
answer questions at the meeting.
The Company counts all proxy votes cast in respect of the Annual 
General Meeting and makes available the proxy voting figures on 
each resolution. The voting results where resolutions are passed 
on a show of hands and details of all proxy votes cast prior to 
the meeting are available on the Company’s website. The results 
of the meeting are announced to the market via a Regulated 
Information Service. This Report to shareholders for the year ended 31 December 2011 
has been prepared in accordance with the relevant provisions of 
the Large and Medium-sized Companies and Groups (Accounts 
and Reports) Regulations 2008 and the applicable Listing Rules. 
A resolution to approve this Report will be proposed at the Annual 
General Meeting of the Company at which the financial statements 
will also be approved. The vote will have an advisory status in respect 
of the remuneration policy and overall remuneration packages and 
will not be specific to individual levels of remuneration. Certain parts 
of this Report are audited. Audited information is stated as such in 
the relevant section.
The remuneration Committee
The Remuneration Committee members are independent, Non-
Executive Directors. The Committee Chairman is Richard Stillwell. 
Its other members are Stephen Dryden and Brian Taylorson. 
No member of the Committee has any personal financial interest 
(other than as a shareholder), conflict of interest arising from cross-
directorships or day-to-day involvement in running the business of 
the Company.
The Committee normally meets no less than three times a year and 
has delegated responsibility for determining and agreeing with the 
Board the framework or broad policy for the remuneration of all 
Executive Directors and other senior executives and for determining, 
within the agreed terms of reference, specific remuneration 
packages for each of the Executive Directors (including pension 
rights), any compensation payments and the operation of executive 
incentive schemes. No director is involved in decisions relating 
to his own remuneration. During the period under review, the 
Remuneration Committee met on six occasions.
The Committee’s full terms of reference, which are available on the 
Company’s website at www.fiberweb.com, are reviewed annually 
and any proposed revisions are referred to the Board for formal 
approval and adoption.
The Committee is responsible inter alia for:
q 	 		 making recommendations to the Board on remuneration policy 
as applied to the Company’s Executive Directors and other 
senior management;
q 	 	determining the remuneration packages for the Executive 
Directors and the company secretary and the framework 
or broad policy for other designated members of executive 
management including base pay, performance-related bonus 
schemes, long-term incentives and other share awards;
q 	 	overseeing major changes in employee benefit structures 
throughout the Group;
q 	 	reviewing the design and operation of all share incentive plans 
for Board and shareholder approval, including approving grants 
of share awards to directors and senior managers; and
q 	 	Reporting to the Board and external stakeholders on matters 
within its responsibilities.
The Committee has appointed New Bridge Street a remuneration 
consultancy, as external advisers. New Bridge Street is a trading 
name of Aon Hewitt Limited, which is part of the Aon Corporation. 
New Bridge Street has provided the Committee with advice in 
respect of certain aspects of main Board and senior executive 
remuneration. New Bridge Street provided no other services to the 
Company however the actuarial practice of Aon Hewitt Limited has 
provided actuarial and accounting assistance to the Company on 
pension schemes. No other services were supplied by any other 
part of Aon Corporation. The Committee has also appointed the 
remuneration practice of PricewaterhouseCoopers to provide 
advice in appropriate circumstances should the need arise. 
PricewaterhouseCoopers provided internal audit and tax advisory 
services to the Company during the year. The remuneration 
practice of PricewaterhouseCoopers operates separately from the 
rest of PricewaterhouseCoopers and there are provisions in place 
to ensure that there is no crossover of information between different 
practice areas. The Committee identified no conflict in the nature of 
services provided by its advisers.
The Committee also consults with the Chairman, who is not a 
member of the Remuneration Committee, the Chief Executive 
Officer and the Head of HR and Change, save in respect of matters 
directly relating to their own remuneration. The Committee receives 
an annual briefing on senior management remuneration and terms 
applicable within the Group and is otherwise appraised of pay and 
conditions in the Group as a whole by the Head of HR and Change 
as necessary to allow the Committee to take such matters into 
account when framing executive remuneration policy.
remuneration Policy
Fiberweb’s remuneration policy is that the remuneration of the 
Company’s Executive Directors and other senior management 
should be designed to attract and retain executives of high calibre 
so that the Company can be managed effectively to the benefit of its 
stakeholders. Remuneration levels are set taking into account the 
remuneration practices found in other UK listed companies of similar 
size, geographical spread and complexity. Consideration  
is also given to the economic realities of the Company’s own  
specific circumstances (in particular the current stage of the 
Company’s development and the international nature of its business 
operations) and remuneration and employment conditions for all 
employees elsewhere in the Group. The Committee is conscious of 
the need to remain competitive in the different geographic  
areas in which the Company operates. In determining its 
remuneration policy, the Committee also takes account of UK 
corporate governance best practice and current market practice.
The remuneration policy of the Company is to pay base salaries and 
total remuneration around the median level for “on-plan” performance 
and to provide the opportunity, via bonuses and long-term incentive 
plans, for executives to be rewarded at the upper quartile for the 
delivery of outstanding levels of performance. The Committee is 
mindful of the dangers of following median remuneration levels and 
conducts external benchmarking less frequently than before.
The Committee has discretion to consider corporate performance 
on environmental, social and governance matters when setting the 
remuneration of Executive Directors but has chosen not to take these 
into account in setting the specific performance targets for 2011 and 
2012. The Committee believes that the structures in place neither 
encourage nor reward inappropriate behaviour in this regard and that 
relevant operational controls relating to such matters are in place. 
HS&E performance remains a key area for the Company.
The Committee considers that the Executive Directors’ remuneration 
packages contain a suitable balance of fixed and variable 
performance-related pay and that the targets set for performance- 
related pay are appropriate and demanding in the context of 
market practice, the Group’s trading environment and the current 
challenges that it faces. Performance-related remuneration forms 
a substantial element of the total remuneration package and 
is designed so as not to encourage excessive risk-taking but 
to be consistent with an approach which seeks to foster the 
generation of sustainable long-term returns for investors. Therefore, 
the Committee is satisfied that the Company’s remuneration 
policy and the Executive Directors’ remuneration packages do 
not encourage inappropriate operational risk taking and do not 
raise environmental, social or governance risks by inadvertently 
motivating irresponsible behaviour.

Directors’ Remuneration Report   Fiberweb PLC  ANNUAL REPORT AND FINANCIAL STATEMENTS 2011    47  
The Committee fully understands and is monitoring government 
proposals on the “clawback” of payments and awards for Executive 
Directors and expects to put arrangements in place once the 
consultation process is complete.
The main elements of the remuneration packages for the Executive 
Directors and senior management are as follows:
q 	 	base salary;
q 	 	benefits in kind;
q 	 	short-term cash based incentives;
q 	 	long-term share based incentives; and
q 	 	pension arrangements.
These elements for the Executive Directors are discussed in 
further detail below.
base Salary
Base salaries are reviewed in relation to market data for 
comparable companies in terms of size, market sector, complexity 
and geographic spread. Reviews generally occur on an annual 
basis and are based on performance, assessment of personal 
objectives where appropriate and any changes in responsibilities.
Daniel Dayan’s base salary for the period under review was 
£382,000 per annum and Daniel Abrams’ base salary for the 
period under review was £227,000 per annum. The total salaries 
received by Daniel Dayan and Daniel Abrams for the year under 
review are shown in Table 1 on page 50. 
Following the sale of the majority of the Group’s hygiene business 
at the end of 2011, Daniel Dayan proposed a reduction in his 
own salary of £50,000 per annum, having regard to the reduced 
scale and complexity of the Group. The Remuneration Committee 
accepted his proposal and accordingly, with effect from 1 March 
2012, Daniel Dayan’s base salary will be reduced to £332,000 
per annum.
As mentioned in the announcement issued on 3 January 2012, 
Daniel Abrams will resign as CFO in March 2012. Kate Miles 
will be appointed to the Board as Group Finance Director upon 
Mr Abrams’ departure and her base salary will be £180,000 per 
annum.
benefits in Kind
Benefits in kind for the Executive Directors include private medical 
insurance, personal accident insurance, permanent health 
insurance and life assurance. The Executive Directors are not 
provided with company cars and do not receive a car allowance.
Short-Term Cash based incentives
The Executive Directors are eligible to participate in the Senior 
Management Bonus Scheme under which payments may 
be made based on the achievement of challenging financial 
targets. Appropriate financial targets are set by the Remuneration 
Committee at the beginning of the financial year for which the 
bonus is payable. As described more fully below, for 2011, 50% 
of the bonus opportunity is payable by reference to performance 
in the first six months of the year with the balance payable by 
reference to performance in the second six months of the year. 
For the Executive Directors however the bonus is only paid 
after the end of the financial year once the Committee has 
had an opportunity to consider performance for the full year.  
The Committee is satisfied that given the particular circumstances 
of the Company the approach to bonus payments is appropriate 
and that there is no likelihood that the aggregate size of bonuses 
payable in any year will not reflect overall Group performance for 
that year.
2011 bonuses
For 2011, the Senior Management Bonus Scheme provided an 
incentive opportunity of up to 100% of base salary for Executive 
Directors. Primarily, 70% of the bonus opportunity was based on 
the achievement of profit after tax targets and 30% of the bonus 
opportunity was based on the achievement of return on capital 
targets, with the Committee then considering performance in the 
round to determine what level of bonus (if any) should be paid. For 
achievement of 95% of budgeted performance under both metrics, 
a bonus of 40% of maximum bonus earning potential was payable.  
For achievement of 100% of budgeted performance under both 
metrics, a bonus of 50% of maximum bonus earning potential 
was payable. Budgeted performance was considered to represent 
challenging targets. In order not to reward underachievement, 
no payout occurs for achievement of below 95% of budget 
performance. In 2011, the Company did not achieve 95% of budget 
performance and based on performance against targets and 
taking account of overall performance in the year, no bonuses were 
paid to the Executive Directors.
2012 bonuses
For 2012, the Senior Management Bonus Scheme will provide a 
bonus opportunity of up to 120% of base salary for Daniel Dayan 
and up to 100% of base salary for Kate Miles. The increase in the 
bonus opportunity for Daniel Dayan from 100% in 2011 to 120% 
in 2012 reflects the reduction in base salary mentioned above and 
his pension reduction mentioned below. The bonus opportunity 
will be measured as follows:
q 	 40% of the bonus opportunity will be measured against underlying 
Group EBIT. There will be a payout of 30% of the maximum 
earning under this metric for achievement of budgeted 
performance and a payout of 100% of the maximum earning 
under this metric for achievement of 120% of budgeted 
performance. The payout for performance between budgeted 
performance and 120% of budgeted performance will be 
determined on a straight-line basis. There will be no payout under 
this metric for achievement of below budgeted performance.
q 	 	30% of the bonus opportunity will be measured against Group 
working capital as a percentage of sales. For all divisional 
managers, there will be a payout of 50% of the maximum earning 
under this metric for achievement of budgeted performance. This 
payout will rise on a straight-line basis so that there will be a 
payout of 100% of the maximum earning potential under this 
metric for achievement of working capital as a percentage of 
sales equal to or greater than 3 basis points below budgeted 
performance. There will be no payout for achievement below 
budgeted performance. The payout for the Executive Directors, 
expressed as a percentage of maximum earning under this 
metric, will be the average (weighted by budgeted external sales) 
of the payouts to divisional managers.
q 	 	30% of the bonus opportunity will be measured against 
personal objectives. There will be a payout of 33.33% of the 
maximum earning under this metric if some of the personal 
objectives are met, 66.67% of the maximum earning potential 
under this metric if most of the personal objectives are met and 
100% of the maximum earning potential under this metric if all 
of the personal objectives are met. There will be no payout if 
none of the personal objectives are met. The Remuneration 
Committee reserves the right to determine the level of payout 
to take account of performance, which may result in a payout 
between the thresholds mentioned above.
The Remuneration Committee has ultimate discretion to assess 
the extent of any payout under the Senior Management Bonus 
Scheme. Notwithstanding the above, there will be no bonus payment under 
the EBIT and working capital metrics to any scheme participants if:
q 	 	the Group’s return on operating assets for the second half of 
the year is less than 10%; or
q 	 the Group’s EBIT for the full year is below £15.1 million.
To the extent that the performance measures are met, payments  
will be made to all scheme participants only after the publication 
of the full year results. This approach gives the Committee the 
opportunity to ensure that the total bonus payable for the year 
reflects the full year Group performance before any actual payment 
is made.
Long-Term Share based incentives
Deferred Share Matching Plan (“DSMP”)
Shareholders approved the DSMP in November 2006 at the time 
of the demerger of the Company from BBA Group plc. Under 
the plan, a maximum of 50% of an executive’s net bonus may be 
voluntarily deferred into shares for three years. The deferred shares 
will then be matched at a rate of one to one (on a gross basis).  
The matching awards will vest three years after grant if and to 
the extent that performance targets attached to the awards are 
satisfied. The detailed targets will be discussed and communicated 
to shareholders in advance of such awards being made.  
No matching awards have so far been made under the DSMP.
Long-Term incentive Plan (“LTiP”)
Shareholders also approved the LTIP in November 2006.  
In summary, under the LTIP, awards over shares with a face value 
of up to 100% of annual salary (200% in exceptional circumstances) 
can be made to Executive Directors in each financial year which (in 
normal circumstances) vest three years after grant, subject to the 
achievement of stretching performance conditions. The exercise 
period in respect of the award expires one year thereafter.
Awards under the LTIP were granted to senior managers  
(including the Executive Directors) in 2006, 2008, 2009 and 2011. 
No awards were granted during 2007 and 2010.
The 2008, 2009 and 2011 awards are subject to total shareholder 
return (“TSR”) and earnings per share (“EPS”) targets. For the 2008 
awards the TSR target was based on absolute total shareholder 
return (see table below) as the Committee considered at the 
relevant time that this was more appropriate in the circumstances 
and provided greater alignment with shareholder interests than 
a relative measure of performance. The EPS target for the 2008 
awards measures EPS for the financial year ended 31 December 
2007 against EPS for the financial year ending 31 December 
2010. For the 2009 and 2011 awards the TSR target is based on 
Fiberweb’s performance relative to the constituents of the FTSE 
SmallCap Index (excluding investment trusts).The EPS target for the 
2009 awards measures EPS for the financial year ended 31 Events 
will be December 2008 against EPS for the financial year ended  
31 December 2011 and for the 2011 awards measures EPS for 
the financial year ended 31 December 2011 against EPS for the 
financial year ending 31 December 2014 (see table below).
These performance conditions were chosen to provide a  
balanced long-term incentive for senior executives to generate both 
above market returns to shareholders and strong levels of EPS growth.
These awards vest as shown in the table below. Sliding scale 
straight line vesting occurs for performance between the relevant 
threshold and maximum targets. LTIP awards (and DSMP awards 
if and when granted) do not have a “re-testing” facility. If the 
performance conditions are not met at the end of the relevant 
performance period, the awards will lapse.
The assessment of fulfilment of the TSR target and relevant TSR 
calculations will be undertaken by independent remuneration 
advisers. The Company’s external auditors will verify the 
Committee’s calculation of the extent to which the EPS targets 
have been met. These methods have been chosen to ensure that

At its meeting on 28 February 2012, the Remuneration Committee 
approved in principle the grant of awards under the LTIP to senior 
managers (including the Executive Directors). The 2012 awards will 
be subject to total shareholder return (“TSR”), earnings per share 
(“EPS”) and return on operating assets (RoOA) targets. The TSR 
target is based on Fiberweb’s performance relative to the constituents 
of the FTSE SmallCap Index (excluding investment trusts). The EPS 
target measures EPS for the financial year ended 31 December 
2012 against EPS for the financial year ended 31 December 2014. 
The RoOA target measures the growth in return on operating assets 
over the three year performance period.
The performance targets applied to future awards will be set by 
the Committee taking into account the outlook for the Company 
at that time and will be fully disclosed in the relevant Directors’ 
Remuneration Report. In addition, the Committee will regularly 
review the operation of the Company’s share based incentive 
arrangements in light of the circumstances and prospects of the 
Company as they develop and emerging trends in market and 
best practice.

executive Share Option Plan (“eSOP”)
The Company established the ESOP following shareholder 
approval in November 2006. Under the ESOP, the normal

in exceptional circumstances). Options will vest after three years,

In 2011 the Company made pension contributions at a rate of 25% 
of base salary to Daniel Dayan which was invested in a defined 
contribution scheme nominated by him. Daniel Abrams also received 
a pension contribution at the rate of 15% of base salary which was 
invested in a defined contribution scheme nominated by him.

at least 7.5% of their salary to the Company defined contribution 
scheme. Details of Company pension contributions made in respect 
of the directors during the year under review are set out in Table 1. 
With effect from 1 March 2012, Mr Dayan’s entitlement to a pension 
supplement will be reduced in line with his reduction in base salary 
by about £12,500 per annum so that his pension contribution  
will continue to be made at a rate of 25% of base salary. Mr Dayan  
will no longer be required to pay into the Company defined 
contribution scheme. Kate Miles will be entitled to a pension

7.5% of her base salary to the Company defined contribution 
scheme.

Awards under Long-Term incentive Plan (“LTiP”) – (audited)
The awards are to be satisfied through a mixture of shares 
purchased in the market and newly issued shares. In accordance 
with the ABI guidelines, the Company operates a 10% in 10 year 
dilution limit for all its share schemes and a 5% in 10 year limit for 
discretionary schemes.
Service Contracts
Daniel Dayan’s service contract dated 27 October 2006 provides 
for 12 months’ notice by either party. In the event of early 
termination by the Company other than for cause, the Company 
may elect to make a single payment in lieu of notice or to make 
the payment in three instalments. The payment will include  
base salary, an assessment of lost bonus opportunity and 
benefits and, to the extent prescribed by the relevant plan rules, 
share award entitlements. If the payment is made in instalments, 
the first instalment is payable on termination and will comprise 
six months’ payment in lieu of notice (calculated to include  
the remuneration elements described above). The second 
and third payments will comprise three months’ notice each.  
The second payment will be made six months after termination 
and the third payment will be made nine months after termination. 
To recognise the duty to mitigate loss the second and  
third instalments will be reduced to take into account the 
remuneration paid pursuant to any alternative employment 
obtained by the executive director prior to such payments 
becoming due.

immediately preceding the date of the 2009 awards was 64.70p. In accordance with the Plan rules the price used to determine the number of nil-cost 
awards made to the Executive Directors on 26 June 2009 was 64.70p.
 3.  The awards dated 26 June 2009 were adjusted by a factor of 1.23 to take account of the rights offer which took place on 18 March 2011.

preceding the date of the 2011 awards was 75.75 pence. In accordance with the Plan rules the price used to determine the number of nil-cost awards 
made to the Executive Directors on 3 May 2011 was 75.75p.

31 December 2011 the highest and lowest prices for Fiberweb shares were 106.50p (2010: 93.75p) and 39.25p (2010: 49.25p) respectively.

Kate Miles’ service contract will provide for 12 months’ notice 
by either party. In the event of early termination by the Company 
other than for cause, the Company may elect to make a single 
payment in lieu of notice or to make the payment by monthly 
instalments. The payment will include base salary, benefits and, 
to the extent prescribed by the relevant plan rules, share award 
entitlements. To recognise the duty to mitigate loss the monthly 
instalments will be reduced to take into account the remuneration 
paid pursuant to any alternative employment obtained by the 
executive director prior to such payments becoming due.
No provision is made for any termination payment in the event of 
early termination for cause and the Committee is conscious of the 
need to protect the Company against the risk of making payments 
in the event of failure whilst having regard to the Company’s legal 
obligations.
Under the terms of a compromise agreement between the 
Company and Daniel Abrams dated 9 January 2012, Mr Abrams’ 
service contract dated 1 February 2008 and his employment by 
the Company will terminate on 31 March 2012.
Mr Abrams is entitled under his service contract to 12 months’ 
notice. As he has remained an employee for 3 months of his 
notice period, he will receive a payment in lieu of notice of the 
balance of 9 months in accordance with his contract and which 
will be paid in two instalments:
q 	 	£173,573.49, which shall be paid within 28 days of the date of 
termination of employment; and
q 	 	£86,786.75, less any income and benefits Mr Abrams has 
derived or could reasonably expect to derive from any 
alternative employment up to and including 31 December 
2012, which shall be paid during October 2012. 
Mr Abrams is subject to an ongoing duty to mitigate by actively 
seeking alternative employment.
Mr Abrams will also receive his salary, holiday pay and benefits up 
to and including 31 March 2012 in accordance with his contract 
and an amount of £30,000 (which includes statutory redundancy) 
as compensation for loss of employment and in respect of UK 
statutory employment rights which shall be paid within 28 days 
of the date of termination of employment. The Company also 
made a contribution to Mr Abram’s legal fees capped at £3,000 in 
connection with his termination arrangements.
The Remuneration Committee determined that no bonus should 
be awarded to Mr Abrams for 2011. Under his service contract 
he is contractually entitled to a bonus of £20,532.50 for the period  
1 January 2012 to 31 March 2012 and this will be paid in April 2012.
Mr Abrams’ 2009 LTIP awards shall vest in accordance with the 
rules of the LTIP if and to the extent that the relevant performance 
targets are met. Only 50% of his 2011 LTIP awards shall vest in 
accordance with the rules of the LTIP, and only if and to the extent 
that the relevant performance targets are met.
Policy on external Directorships
The Board believes that the experience gained by Executive 
Directors through their involvement with other companies could 
be of benefit to the individual director and the Company. 
Executive Directors are, with the Board’s permission, allowed to 
accept one such appointment, as long as there is no conflict of 
interest and the time commitment involved does not undermine 
the performance of their duties at the Company. The executive 
director may keep the fees from his external appointment. 
Neither of the Executive Directors currently holds a non-executive 
appointment.
Non-executive Directors’ remuneration
The original appointment of the Chairman was for a period expiring 
at the end of the Annual General Meeting in 2010. His letter of 
appointment dated 19 October 2006 and amended by a letter dated 
29 October 2009 has been extended by a letter dated 29 April 2010 
until the close of the Annual General Meeting of the Company in 
2013. His appointment letters are available for inspection on request.
The appointment of each of Richard Stillwell and Brian Taylorson 
as Non-Executive Directors was for an initial term of three 
years effective from the date of demerger in November 2006.  
The letters of appointment of Richard Stillwell and Brian Taylorson 
are dated 19 October 2006 and their appointments have been 
extended by letters each dated 29 April 2010 until the close of 
the Annual General Meeting of the Company in 2013. The letter 
of appointment of Stephen Dryden as a Non-Executive Director is 
dated 27 May 2009 and his appointment is for a period of three 
years from 1 June 2009 until 31 May 2012. The current letters 
of appointment for all the Non-Executive Directors are available 
for inspection on request. The Non-Executive Directors do not 
participate in any Company’s pension arrangements or incentive 
plans. Appointments can be terminated by either party on three 
months’ notice or compensation, and six months’ notice or 
compensation in the case of the Chairman.
The level of fees for the Non-Executive Directors is determined 
by the Board as a whole on the recommendation of the 
Chairman and the Executive Directors. The Chairman’s fees are 
determined by the Board as a whole on the recommendation 
of the Remuneration Committee after consulting with the Chief 
Executive Officer. Fees are in line with current market practice of 
comparable organisations and are set taking account of the time 
commitment and responsibility of each Non-Executive Director. 
The Chairman’s base annual fee is £120,000 per annum having 
been increased by £10,000 per annum on 1 November 2009. 
The base annual fee for Non-Executive Directors is £32,000. 
The Chairmen of the Audit and Remuneration Committees each 
receive an annual supplement of £6,000 in recognition of the 
increased commitment placed upon them in performing their 
roles. Richard Stillwell does not receive an additional supplement 
for his role as Senior Independent Director.
Fees for the Chairman and Non-Executive Directors have been 
regularly reviewed and remained unchanged during 2011. Details 
of Non-Executive Directors’’ fees for 2011 are set out in Table 1 
on page 50.
